Famine in Shunde and Zhongshan Counties of Guangdong Province: Rural Bankruptcy, Starvation Everywhere, Local People Collect Funds and Provide Congee 89

Guangzhou Correspondence: Shunde, Zhongshan, and other counties in Guangdong Province have always been dominated by silk exports. Unexpectedly, in recent years, the silk industry has declined, and silk exports have almost been cut off. In the past, silk exports were worth more than 2,000 yuan per package, but now each package (about 100 catties) has dropped to 200 yuan, and no one cares. As a result, silkworm farmers have lost their jobs, the rural economy has gone bankrupt, the old and weak have died in ditches, and the young and strong have scattered in all directions. Selling children and daughters is heard every day. Most of the female workers have also gone to Nanyang to temporarily make a living. At present, mulberry fields are barren and the sound of looms has stopped. Recently, although the promotion of changing mulberry fields to plant miscellaneous grains has been advocated, the harvest is limited, and the product prices are low, and the farmers' difficulties are increasing day by day. For several months, there has been famine in various villages, and the starved people are everywhere. The elders of the various villages have witnessed the tragic situation, and they have discussed and mortgaged the old properties of the ancestral halls in various villages to wealthy families for cash, and distributed the cash to relieve the famine victims. Those who have implemented it are the Xinji Li clan in Beixiang, who have relieved 2 yuan per person to maintain the current food. In addition, the Long clan in Nanxiang, the Hu clan in Guizhouxiang, the Yang clan, Guan clan, Peng clan in Rongqixiang, the Long clan, Luo clan in Daliang, etc. are all in order to relieve the famine. Since the 23rd of last month, the number of famine victims receiving relief rice in Daliang Famine Relief Office has increased day by day. On the 25th, there were more than 13,000 people. The relief office temporarily built more than 20 feet of sunflower sheds to handle the relief affairs. In the past few days, 123680 and other districts have been waiting for relief in Daliang. There are no fewer than 5,000 people a day. The Chencun Relief Association in the county has recently set up a second distribution point in Zhengangxiang because of the increasing number of famine victims. In the past five days, 6,100 refugees have registered in Xinxu, and 8,200 refugees have registered in Jiuxu, totaling more than 14,000 famine victims. However, the financial resources of the rural clans are limited and it is difficult to maintain for a long time. It is still necessary for the local charities and the government to allocate funds to provide relief.

Zhongshan County was originally called a model county and was known for its wealth. The county's output is mainly rice, and the Xiaolan area is also a silk-producing area. Recently, the situation has changed greatly. Grain is cheap and hurts farmers, and the silk industry has plummeted. The rural economy has collapsed, and famine victims are everywhere in the districts. Zhongshan wealthy businessmen living in Hong Kong are concerned about the disaster victims. A Hong Kong Overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce Relief Association was established in Hong Kong a few days ago to raise funds and purchase 5,000 bags of rice in Hong Kong. They were transported back to the county to hold emergency relief. On the 24th of last month, the first batch of 704 bags of relief rice were set up in Shiqi at the Zhongshan Overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce Relief Office, providing congee and selling rice at a low price. Congee and low-priced rice sales began on the 28th of last month. For the time being, 1,000 bags of relief rice were used for congee in various districts, and 3,400 bags of relief rice were used for low-priced rice sales in various districts. The number of famine victims in each district was checked, and the first district was about 15,000 people, the second district was 20,000 people, the third district was 50,000 people, the fourth district was 15,000 people, the seventh district was 15,000 people, and the ninth district was 50,000 people. Regarding congee, the distribution of relief rice in each district is as follows: 90 bags in the first district, 20 bags in the second district, 300 bags in the third district, 90 bags in the fourth district, 90 bags in the seventh district, and 300 bags in the ninth district, totaling 320,000 catties. The township office in each district will first investigate the number of famine victims in each district, and then hand over the relief rice to the township head for distribution. The amount of relief rice is the same for men, women, old and young. As for the low-priced rice sales, it is presided over by the Zhongshan Chamber of Commerce. The allocation of low-priced rice per stone is estimated to be 306 bags in the first district, 408 bags in the second district, 1,000 bags in the third district, 306 bags in the fourth district, 306 bags in the seventh district, and 1,000 bags in the ninth district. The deadline for low-priced rice sales is one month. The township office in each district will first submit a letter reporting the number of famine victims in that place. Each time, the purchase of rice is only allowed to be enough for the famine victims to use for ten days, and no more can be purchased to avoid the latecomers being left out. Disaster victims who buy rice must first receive a low-priced rice voucher. The voucher states the amount of rice limited to each meal, and each person cannot exceed half a catty at a time, and each person is only allowed to buy two meals a day, and no more can be bought to limit it. (July 29)

Wuxi: The Labor Strike at Zhenxin Mill is Becoming More Serious 91

The Zhenxin Cotton Mill in Taibaodun, outside the West Gate of the city, had a go-slow strike on the 31st of last month due to unpaid wages. Later, through the efforts of the party and government officials and the public security authorities, and the mill manager, Jiang Zeqing, also asked Cai Jiansan, chairman of the Cotton Textile Industry Association, to represent him, he told the party and government officials that he would first pay the first installment of wages on the 5th. The rest would be paid off successively. The strike came to an end. The 1st was the mill's holiday. On the morning of the 2nd, the mill suddenly issued a notice saying that the mill would be temporarily suspended for internal repairs. The workers were afraid that the suspension of work would affect the livelihoods of all the workers, and they were shocked and angry. They went to Jiang Zeqing's residence in Shipixiang to question him. Because Jiang was sick and unable to walk, he was at Puren Hospital, so they went to Puren Hospital to surround him. The dean of the hospital, Li Kele, saw that the situation was tense and was afraid that something else would happen, so he urgently called the Public Security Bureau to send Inspector Wang and the chief of the first branch to suppress the situation. After finding out that Jiang Zeqing was indeed sick, he tried to persuade the workers to disperse and wait for mediation. Yesterday (the 3rd) morning, County Magistrate Wang invited Xu Chizi, executive member of the County Party Department, Director Chen of the Public Security Bureau, Cai Jiansan, chairman of the Cotton Textile Industry Association, and Hua Shaochun, the representative of labor and management, to jointly negotiate. However, at this time, the flower is expensive and the yarn is cheap, the money is tight, the internal management is difficult, and the external market is affected. The pain suffered by the factory cannot be easily solved. County Magistrate Wang invited Qian Sunqing, the president of the Chamber of Commerce, and the presidents of the Bank of China and the Bank of Shanghai to conduct thorough consultations at the Chamber of Commerce. There are thorough solutions, and it is not difficult to continue to start work.

Grain Merchants Collect Business Tax on Wheat on Behalf of the Bureau 92

The Business Tax Bureau of this county has recently received instructions from the Provincial Department that all grain merchants who purchase snacks on behalf of customers must collect temporary business tax on their behalf. Flour mills that have paid the general tax and purchase wheat raw materials in the place of production exclusively for the use of the mill are allowed to be tax-free if they do not engage in sales activities. If the flour mills entrust the grain merchants to purchase them indirectly on their behalf, the business tax should be paid by the grain merchants on their behalf. Director Xia has issued an order to the Rice Bean and Miscellaneous Grain Association to order the grain merchants to handle it.

Silk Market Improves, Silk Mills Go-Slow One After Another 94

Yichang Silk Mill in Nanqiao Town, the third district, started operations in May of this year, with a total of 256 silk machines. Wang Jiliang, the director of the mill, recently extended the working hours in order to speed up production because the silk market has improved. The wages were paid at 75% of the original rate, which caused dissatisfaction among the female workers in the entire mill. At 0:30 pm on the 2nd, they went on a go-slow strike. On the one hand, they sent representatives to the factory to request a reduction in working hours and to implement six in and six out (that is, work at 6 am and leave work at 6 pm). The wages must be paid in full and no discounts are allowed. As a result, the factory decided that the working hours would still be handled according to the past regulations, and the wages would be paid as usual. The workers were satisfied, so they resumed work yesterday (the 3rd) morning. Also, the Qianxin No. 1 and No. 2 mills in Gongyun Bridge and Beixin Bridge went on a go-slow strike because they changed to full-day work. After mediation, it was decided to do half-day work during this hot summer, and the strike was calmed down.

Changshu: Tofu Industry Strike 95

The tofu industry in this county suddenly went on strike on the 2nd. It is said that the purpose is to jointly discuss the price increase issue. Although the tofu industry is a small business, there are many people who eat it. The general public regards it as the only side dish. However, the industry has no organization. Recently, due to the high price of beans and the increased cost, it is difficult to maintain. Therefore, it is planned to organize an association this time, named Minxin Tang, and to negotiate and set the industry rules. After this, each board of tofu will be 560 yuan, each piece of tofu will be 20 yuan, each oil bubble will be 5 yuan, each page of tofu skin will be 50 yuan, and each piece of dried tofu will be 20 yuan. All stores must not differ. It is reported that it has been approved by the industry, and the strike will last for three days to facilitate reorganization. The resumption of business is approved from the 5th, but the general public has felt inconvenience in recent days.

Jiading: The Reaction to the Rectification of Housing Tax 97

The county government, upon receiving the provincial order to rectify the housing tax, convened a meeting of leaders from various agencies and groups on July 26th to discuss implementation methods, but no concrete results were achieved. Local groups continued to meet on the 31st at the county party headquarters, stating that: (1) the provincial order to implement the housing tax was for the purpose of funding public security expenses, but the county's public security expenses have long been levied on farmland, which is more than sufficient, surpassing neighboring counties significantly, making it unnecessary to implement a housing tax; (2) Nanxiang, a town in the county, has previously collected donations from shops for public welfare purposes, but this was voluntary and without a fixed tax rate, and it was abolished after July last year, so there is no housing tax now, making rectification unnecessary; (3) the county has suffered repeated major disasters and warfare, and the people's resources are strained and unable to bear additional burdens. It was decided to jointly petition the Ministry of Finance, the provincial government, the Provincial Department of Finance, and the Provincial Tax Supervisory Council through the Jiading and Nanxiang Chambers of Commerce, various trade guilds, and the County Education Association for exemption from the tax.

Yangzhou: Daylight Robbery Outside the West Gate 98

Although Sao Gou Mountain outside the West Gate of Yangzhou is close to both urban and rural areas, its remote location means few pedestrians in the afternoon, leading to frequent robberies. Today (the 2nd), at around 3:00 PM, Li Youchang, a farmer from Ganquan Mountain in the western countryside, who went to Shanghai for work due to the autumn famine, returned to the town yesterday (the 1st). He crossed the river to Guazhou in the morning and walked back. On the way, he met two people who claimed to be visiting relatives in Ganquan Mountain, so he joined them. Unexpectedly, when they reached a depression in Sao Gou Mountain, one person tightly hugged Li's waist while the other pointed a gun to silence him, taking all twenty-five silver dollars accumulated in Li's pocket. Seeing the gun, Li dared not shout or chase. The bandits fled back and reported to the city gate police at the West Gate, who reported it to the bureau. By the time the detective team was dispatched to investigate the scene, the perpetrators were long gone.

At the home of Ji Yuanwan, a resident of the northern border of Jingou Town in the eighth district of this county, more than ten bandits suddenly arrived the night before, each armed with guns, broke down the door and thoroughly searched the place. Funing: Appointed Judge Acquitted on Appeal 101

Lei Yinghuan, the former appointed judge of Funing County, was sued by Chen Junqing, a litigant, to the Jiangsu High Court Prosecutor's Office for falsifying public documents while in office, which was then referred to the Wuxian District Court for trial. Ningbo: Six More Money Shops in Ningbo City Close Down 102

The Ningbo money industry has recently been affected by the social and economic downturn, leading to the successive announcements of closure and liquidation of five major money shops: Datong, Xingyuan, Xinyuan, Taiyuan, and Yongsheng, as well as two smaller shops: Wuyuan and the current exchange shop, Hui Da. Unexpectedly, four more money shops, Hengmao, Xingyuan, Weikang, and Yankang, ran aground and closed shop the day before yesterday (the 1st). This is truly a misfortune for society. The Yin County government, considering the widespread rumors, specifically established measures yesterday to maintain stability, limiting depositors to withdrawals of no more than one hundred yuan, and publicized this widely, while also consulting with the Chamber of Commerce to discuss relief measures. The Chamber of Commerce has scheduled a meeting for 2:00 PM today (the 2nd) to convene both the silver and money industries to discuss ways to maintain the market. However, with the onset of such a crisis, the entire situation is in turmoil, making it difficult to contain it immediately. Today (the 2nd), six more major money shops, Jingyuan, Huiyuan, Yuyuan, Yuanheng, Yufeng, and Ruiyu, have closed down and are undergoing liquidation. If effective relief measures are not devised in concert, the future of the local money industry is fraught with hidden reefs, leaving little room for optimism. For days, people have been restless. Deposits at the Bank of China have increased by more than two million yuan in the past two days, demonstrating the shift in power between money and banking.

Local News

Xu Shiying Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday and Makes a Statement: Currently Consulting with Shanghai Leaders to Plan Relief Efforts 103

According to the Central News Agency, Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Central Relief Commission, arrived in Shanghai by Jiang'an wheel at noon on the 2nd, arriving at the dock around 8 AM on the 3rd, and made the following statement:

I sincerely hope that the people of Shanghai will economize on food and clothing.

I inspected the flood-stricken areas of Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui, departing from Shanghai on July 15th and returning to the capital on the 28th. All public reports have already been printed yesterday. All relief measures have been submitted to the Executive Yuan and handed over to the Ministries of Interior and Finance, the Department of Health, and the Relief Commission for review, with the Economic Commission also participating. Detailed content cannot be disclosed for the time being. However, the floods in the provinces are extremely severe. The Sixth and Seventh Administrative Inspectorate Districts of Hubei Province are even worse than in the 20th year. The people of Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan are still in deep water, and Tianmen is almost submerged, with the number of deaths estimated to be sixty to seventy percent. A total of 51 out of 70 counties in Hubei Province have been affected by the disaster. 37 out of 76 counties in Hunan Province have been affected, especially Xiangxi, Lixian, Linli, Shimen, Cili, and Anxiang counties. The remaining 49 out of 83 counties in Jiangxi and 13 out of 60 counties in Anhui are also disaster areas, affecting 14 million people. A small amount of relief funds cannot provide universal aid. Although Shanghai society is in extreme depression, I sincerely hope that everyone will economize on food and clothing and donate according to their ability. Our people have always been known throughout the world for their disaster relief, neighborly compassion, and kindness. In recent years, Shanghai has demonstrated this to the world and is leading the nation. This disaster is no less severe than before, and I hope that Shanghai will do even more to comfort the disaster victims.

Inspecting the Yellow River Disaster in a Week

Moreover, the five years of famine and the addition of the drought in the Yangtze River basin last year amidst the continuous floods show that the lack of human efforts in recent decades has reached its extreme. To avoid disasters in the future, we must think about fundamental water management. I have some ideas, which I have drafted into a memorial to the central government for consideration. As for the Yellow River flood, it has been reported to be extremely severe in recent days. After consulting with Shanghai authorities and leaders from all walks of life on relief efforts for a week, I will personally go to inspect the situation.

Disaster Relief Committee Concurrently Handles Relief Commission Affairs

As for the Central Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Management Committee, it has been established and the permanent disaster relief reserve fund system can be realized. I am deeply gratified. The committee is ordered to be concurrently managed by the Relief Commission, and all staff members hold concurrent positions without any expenses or subsidies. In recent days, some people have been seeking employment, not understanding the situation.

After Xu finished speaking, he showed a list of the four disaster-stricken provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui, which is transcribed below: (Hubei) Originally 71 counties and cities, 51 counties and cities affected by the disaster. National Labor Representatives Wang Jinxia Returns Home and Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday, Advisor Wu Wentian Arrives on the Same Ship, Reports to Beijing Tonight 109

According to the Central News Agency, Wang Jinxia, the labor representative, and Wu Wentian, the advisor, who attended the 19th International Labor Conference, returned to Shanghai on the Italian mail ship Conte Verde at 2:00 PM yesterday. The National Labor Conference was held in Geneva on June 4th and closed on the 25th. Except for the government representative, Li Pingheng, who remains in Geneva, the employer representatives, Wang Zhisheng and Zhang Hualian, went to the United States together to investigate industries, while Zhang Daomin and Gu Bingyuan also went to Germany and Italy together to study labor. Wang and Wu made the following remarks while still on board:

Conference Situation

More member countries attended this year's conference than in previous years, because the work of the Labor Bureau is valued by countries around the world. Furthermore, new member countries such as Afghanistan, the Soviet Union, and the United States attended this year, and Egypt, a non-member country, also sent representatives to the conference and was allowed to attend as observers with the permission of the conference. The chairman of this year's conference was Mr. Clay Swart, the Minister of Labor of the Government of the Union of South Africa, and the vice-chairmen of the conference were Beck, the government representative of Norway, Mansier, the employer representative of Romania, and Huo Xia, the worker representative of France. The advancement of the conference affairs was assisted by ten major committees. The conference spent the first to fourth sessions busy electing the chairman and vice-chairmen, establishing committees, and electing committee members. It was not until the fifth session that the conference officially began discussions.

Discussion of Proposals

The agenda of this year's conference was more extensive than in the past. For example, the issue of youth unemployment was particularly urgent, so the conference decided to adopt a single-level discussion system and produce a recommendation to be sent to the governments of member countries for reference. As for the issue of reducing working hours, it had been raised for discussion at the 17th and 18th conferences. Employers, with the exception of Italy, all tried their best to oppose it. When the conference discussed this issue, the attitude of the employers was the same as in the past, and the chairman of the employer group announced to the conference that the employer group refused to attend the committee in order to avoid detailed discussions on the issue. For a time, the atmosphere at the conference was extremely tense. In order to facilitate communication, the conference was adjourned for more than ten days. Our country's labor representatives were well aware of the domestic situation, so although they did not want employers to have a sense of threat, the employer representative, Wang Zhisheng, was also able to understand everything. After several debates, some draft conventions on reducing working hours were finally passed. Furthermore, issues such as prohibiting women from working underground in mines, maintaining the insurance benefits due to workers after relocation, and vested rights were all discussed and resulted in conventions to be sent to the governments of member countries for approval. The Convention on Limiting Working Hours in Coal Mines was also amended. As for the two issues of paid vacations and the recruitment of workers in colonies, only preliminary discussions were held this year, and the results remain to be determined by the next conference.

Approval of Conventions

The conference attaches great importance to whether the conventions approved by member countries are strictly enforced. The results of the review of the conventions that our country's government has already approved were deemed satisfactory by this conference. Countries such as Spain, on the other hand, were severely criticized. The committee of the conference that specializes in reviewing the implementation of conventions in various countries is called the Article 408 Committee, and its name is derived from its composition based on the provisions of Article 408 of the Treaty of Versailles. This year, Mr. Wu Wentian was appointed as one of the members of the committee.

Temporary Proposals

Although few temporary proposals were passed, they all had considerable value. However, the Asian Labor Advisory Conference (note: not the Asian Workers' Conference), which is closely related to our Asian workers, was presented with the unanimous support of our country's government and labor representatives. Furthermore, Bao Huaguo and Wu Wentian successively took the stage to give speeches, making every effort to promote the importance of the conference. However, due to insufficient voters during the vote, it failed to pass, which is regrettable.

Opposing Dumping

A total of 159 representatives from the government, labor, and employer sides attended this year's conference, and a total of 255 advisors from the three sides. The qualifications of the representatives were questioned in the case of the worker representatives of Italy, Austria, Cuba, the Union of South Africa, and Bulgaria, and the qualifications of the labor advisors were also questioned in the case of Italy, Austria, and South Africa. Regarding the prevention of dumping, when discussing the report of the Director of the International Labor Office on this matter, the labor representative of our country spoke to the conference and raised this issue, saying that China's modern industry is relatively backward. Today, factories of all sizes are deeply harmed by the dumping policies of the great powers, which makes it impossible for them to maintain operations and puts them in a precarious situation. The serious unemployment problem is thus further exacerbated. Finally, he said that international forces should be used to stop such unfair actions. At the time, the listeners were all moved.

Factory Inspection

Regarding the issue of factory inspection in the concessions, government and labor representatives from various countries have spoken at the conference about its advantages and disadvantages. Later, a meeting was convened by the International Labor Office to specifically discuss this issue. Representatives from the relevant governments of the United Kingdom, the United States, France, and Japan attended. The atmosphere at the time was excellent, but continued efforts are still needed to achieve concrete results.

Reporting to Beijing Tonight

The delegation from our country gave many speeches at the conference. Most of the materials were collected from various agencies and groups by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. However, the National Academic Advisory Committee (regarding the relief of youth unemployment), the China Branch of the International Labor Office, the Geneva International Library, the International Labor Office Library, and the League of Nations Library provided assistance in various ways, which is very commendable. However, the statistical materials were still insufficient, which is regrettable. It is reported that Wang and Wu are scheduled to take the night express train to Beijing tonight to report on everything. Wang Jinxia will soon return to Wuhan by transportation.

Inspection Record of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway: 139 Kilometers in Total, Round Trip Takes 5.3 Hours 112

Since the construction of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway began, the project has progressed rapidly. The entire line, stretching 139 kilometers from Wuxi to the North Railway Station in Shanghai, is now complete. The opening ceremony is scheduled for the 15th of this month at Guyi Garden in Nanxiang, and the highway will officially open for business on the 16th. Our reporter, recognizing the significant cultural and economic importance of this road to the Wuxi-Suzhou-Changzhou area, and aware of the general public's interest in the road's engineering, facilities, and sightseeing opportunities along the route, departed from Shanghai at 6:30 AM on the 2nd to inspect the entire route, returning to Shanghai at 8:30 PM. In addition to the daily round-trip schedules, fare rates for the entire line and branch lines, and regulations for attracting merchants to station services along the route, which were published in yesterday's newspaper, the reporter's observations are compiled below.

Solid Construction

The entire line, totaling 139 kilometers from Qujiang Road in Zhabei, Shanghai, to the northeast end of the Wuxi Railway Station, has a wide road surface and very solid construction. The road surface is paved with gravel, making it very smooth, and the ride is free from any bumping. However, there are quite a few bridges along the entire line. When crossing bridges, if the car's speed exceeds 40 yards, there is a slight bump. There are approximately two hundred and several tens of bridges along the entire line. After investigating the cause of the bumps when crossing bridges, it was found that it is actually due to the uneven connection between the road surface and the bridge at both ends. It is hoped that the company will find a way to improve this.

Itinerary Arrangement

If traveling from Shanghai by private car, it takes half an hour to reach Nanxiang. "When passing through Nanxiang, there are four roads for cars. The northernmost one leads to Nanxiang Town, the southernmost one leads to Nanxiang Railway Station, the road on the right in the middle is the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway, and the one on the left is the Shanghai-Suzhou Highway." It takes only 15 minutes from Nanxiang to Jiading, and about 18 minutes from the West Gate of Jiading to the West Gate of Taicang. It takes 55 minutes from Taicang to Changshu. From Shanghai to Changshu is 95 kilometers, and the driving time is at most two hours. After arriving in Changshu, there are three roads: heading north directly reaches the South Gate of Changshu, a distance of one kilometer; heading south directly leads to Suzhou, a distance of 39 kilometers; heading west is the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway, directly leading to Wuxi, a distance of 44 kilometers. The driving time is about 45 minutes, and you can directly reach the Wuxi Railway Station. Therefore, from Shanghai to Wuxi, if you do not stop along the way, the one-way travel time only takes 2 hours and 45 minutes, and the round trip takes only 5 hours and 30 minutes.

Scenery Along the Way

The civilization and prosperity of the city ultimately cannot compare to the elegance and interest of the countryside. Therefore, after the reporter's car passed Zhenru Town, the flourishing agricultural produce on both sides, the green waves, made one feel refreshed and happy. There are many scenic spots along the way, but due to the short time, it was regrettable that there was no time to stop and visit Nanxiang, Jiading, Taicang, and other places. Upon reaching the South Gate of Changshu, having long admired the scenic beauty of Yushan Mountain, the reporter, along with Mr. Hu Bozhou, the pictorial editor of this newspaper, and Mr. Xu Tianzhang, the photographer, took a rickshaw to the southern foot of Yushan Mountain (rickshaw fare: one silver dollar), to a place called Shimei. There are several teahouses and restaurants there, as well as a Yushan Hotel, which is quite clean. The reporters hastily climbed the mountain, and after about 15 minutes, they reached Xin Feng Pavilion and Qian Yuan Palace at the top of the mountain (this is Yushan Mountain within the city, which is less than one percent of Yushan Mountain outside the city). Looking down from the pavilion, there is West Lake to the west and an ancient pagoda to the north. The dense population can be seen at a glance. They took photos together as a souvenir. After descending the mountain, they rested for a while at a Xin Teahouse, enjoyed some tea and snacks. The teahouse's facilities were quite good, with calligraphy, painting, musical instruments, and chess all available. The tea price was very cheap, only seven copper coins per serving. Next to the tea room was a lotus pond, where the lotus flowers were in full bloom, and the fragrance was refreshing. According to tea drinkers sitting nearby, no fewer than hundreds of local residents come here every day to drink tea and read newspapers, especially in the spring. However, Shanghai newspapers here are not delivered until after 2:00 PM, which feels very slow. It is expected that this will be improved after the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway opens. The reporters originally planned to visit the scenic spots outside the city, such as Yushan Sword Gate and West Lake. Sword Gate is the most famous scenic spot on Yushan Mountain, but it requires walking or taking a sedan, and it takes a lot of time to go back and forth, so they gave up. At 11:40 AM, they departed from the South Gate of Changshu. The lotus flowers on both sides were in full bloom, with red and white colors intertwined, forming a beautiful scene. The road surface from Changshu to Wuxi was wider. They arrived in Wuxi at 12:25 PM, refueled, and drove straight to Meiyuan Garden. After lunch at the Taihu Hotel, they visited Jin Garden, which is operated by the Rong family, next to Taihu Lake. The magnificence of Taihu Lake's shape and the beauty of its scenery are truly rare. It was a pity that they were limited by time and could not cross to Longtouzhu on the opposite side. They took several photos in Jin Garden and then returned. On the way back, they also visited Huishan Mountain and bought several clay toys. At 3:30 PM, they returned to Wuxi from Huishan and drove straight back. At 5:00 PM, they passed Changshu and took the Changshu-Suzhou Highway south. At 5:40 PM, they arrived in Suzhou and refueled again. They toured until 6:30 PM and then took the Suzhou-Shanghai Highway back to Shanghai. At 7:10 PM, they arrived in Kunshan. At 8:00 PM, they passed Nanxiang. At 8:30 PM, they arrived at the North Railway Station. In total, the driving time for this trip was about 6 hours and 15 minutes, and they used 19 gallons of gasoline.

Toll Collection

After the road officially opens, business cars traveling on this road and passing the Green Willow Bridge at the provincial and municipal boundary will still be charged a toll. The amount has not yet been determined, but private cars are exempt.

The members of this committee are either leaders in the business community or financial experts with rich experience. Please give guidance at any time, and do your best to assist in the investigation. Because this matter is important and related to the progress of this committee, it will not be successful without concerted efforts. (5) Training Team Director Luo Qinghua reported on the progress of the first subgroup meeting. Reviving Industry and Commerce: Self-Reliance Should Be Sought, Pan Yisan's Proposal to the Coal Industry Association 114

Mr. Pan Yisan, general manager of North China Coal Company, presented five proposals to the Coal Industry Association of this city yesterday, which are recorded as follows: Our industry and commerce have been in an economically difficult environment for nearly a year. Although each of us has endured hardships and faced the situation calmly, it is ultimately a temporary solution that can only support us for a while and cannot avoid the final result of stopping and closing down. If we investigate the cause in detail, although there are intricate and complex causes, the lack of bargaining chips and the outflow of silver have become the motive for the decline of industry and commerce. Therefore, the response is sluggish, the survivors are worried, and the trend of withdrawing savings deposits has started. The more intense this trend, the more the overall credit standing of industry and commerce collapses, which is the biggest main reason. Because of the collapse of credit, commercial goods are accumulated, and commodity prices plummet. As a result, the rich become poor, and the poor die, gradually heading towards the same end. The economic turnover is like a wheel that can be turned by a ring. How can a wheel with a flaw move? The only way to do it now is to recognize the meaning of coexistence and common prosperity to avoid the danger of the same end. Our industrialists and businessmen must seek their own ways to survive, so that they can continue their dying lives, and the way of self-seeking is nothing more than the self-reliance and regeneration of our industry and commerce. According to the industrial and commercial operations, there is its inherent self-reliance. The so-called self-reliance, in addition to capital, is the commercial credit between each other, and is based on the circulation of commercial goods. Following this principle to seek self-help, there are only three methods: controlling commercial goods, evaluating commodity prices, and generating credit instruments. If the control is successful, the economic capacity exists; if the commodity prices are stable, the self-reliance is solid; if the instruments are in circulation, the turnover is active. This is the way for industry and commerce to save themselves, and it is also possible. It is related to the survival of industry and commerce and the overall situation of our industry. Therefore, the following five methods are proposed, and I dare to ask the conference to make a decision: (1) Handle acceptance drafts (form instructions can be obtained from the City Chamber of Commerce). (2) Handle circulating pledges and fixed-term pledges (contact the City Chamber of Commerce Revival Committee). (3) Discuss and determine the evaluation regulations (stabilize commodity prices and protect the rights and interests of fellow traders). (4) Revise the industry regulations (clarify the rights and interests of our industry, correct malpractices, and promote the degree of revival of the industry). (5) Revise the articles of association (strictly clarify the procedures for joining the association and stabilize the business scope of fellow traders).

Assistance to Overseas Chinese in Siam Association: Standing Committee Meeting Held Yesterday 116

We should unite all sectors of the country to expand the organization, work together, and earnestly assist in order to achieve twice the result with half the effort. (Resolution) Send letters to overseas Chinese groups in Guangzhou, Shantou, Hong Kong, Xiamen, and other places to select and send two responsible representatives to Shanghai to discuss the organization of a national assistance to overseas Chinese in Siam Joint Association in order to concentrate efforts and facilitate the process. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram to the Ministry of Finance: Please Approve the Registration of Old Stamps Quickly 121

Although the Exchange Is Stipulated to Start in July, the Registration of Old Stamps Has Not Been Approved

After the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce received the six articles of the Ministry of Finance's Measures for the Exchange of Old Stamps, it organized an office to start handling it. However, the second article of the exchange measures has the words "old stamp tax tickets that have been approved and registered." Therefore, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting the approval of the registration of old stamps in Shanghai as soon as possible in order to implement the exchange. The original telegram said: Nanjing Ministry of Finance, On July 27, the Ministry sent a telegram to the association issuing six articles of the Measures for the Exchange of Old Stamps. The association immediately gathered the old tickets, met with the members sent by the provincial bureau, and sealed them for safekeeping in accordance with the measures. It has sent a letter to the bureau, requesting it to send a member to the association to handle this procedure from August 1. Now, the bureau has replied that all 1,022 registration application forms from Shanghai merchants have been investigated, registered, and forwarded after meeting with the members of the Ministry, but no order has been received. The matter of jointly checking and sealing the old tickets should be handled in accordance with the second article of the Exchange Measures. After the order is approved, we will send a letter to notify you to do so. The registration of old stamps in Shanghai has been completed for more than half a year. I have heard that the measures issued by the Ministry can be exchanged from July, which is a comfort to the merchants. They originally intended to exchange for new tickets immediately, but they did not know that there were many twists and turns in the collection and verification. When can they exchange for new tickets? There is no definite date. The procedures for official offices are not understood by ordinary merchants, but they know that the Ministry can exchange them from July, but in reality it is still indefinite. They cannot avoid blaming the Chamber of Commerce for delaying. Now, even the meeting and verification procedures cannot be carried out because the provincial bureau has not received an order. This matter is even more distant and indefinite. The business community feels even more disappointed. Therefore, I will send another telegram to the Ministry, requesting that it be quickly approved, so that the provincial bureau can be notified to send personnel to meet and verify as soon as possible. This is a public feeling. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Jiangsu Construction Department Checks and Accepts River Dredging in Counties 123

The general mobilization of river dredging in Shanghai County last year has completed the dredging of all the newly dredged rivers. After inspecting the seven rivers, including Tangchun Jing and Liulei Tang, the staff returned to the department and reported that they were generally able to meet the standards. However, the outer section of the East and West Jiagou at the Huangpu River was too shallow and blocked, and measures should be taken to dredge it as soon as possible to facilitate discharge and navigation. In addition, the section dredged outside the Yingdou River at the Huangpu River and a section near Tangzi Jing were still too shallow and blocked, and the original contractor should be ordered to dredge it in accordance with the plan. In addition, the bottom of the new river was too high to meet the regulations. For example, the West Jiagou was about 2 centimeters high, the North section of Zigang was about 3 centimeters high, the Sunjia Jing was about 2 centimeters high, and the X港 was about 1 to 3 centimeters high. After receiving the report, the department has ordered the Shanghai County Government to immediately supervise the implementation and report, and to pay attention to dredging at any time.

Islamic Missionary Society Representative, Yin Guangyu, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 125

Yin Guangyu, representative of the Chinese Islamic Missionary Society, who last year represented the Society and Mr. Ma Junpu to travel abroad, perform the Hajj to Mecca, and investigate all cultural undertakings, has now been gone for ten months. Mr. Yin arrived in Shanghai yesterday (the 3rd) aboard the Italian mail ship "Conte Verde." Those who went to welcome him included Ma Puqing and Su Zixiang, representatives of the Chinese Islamic Society; Ma Fuying, representative of the Chinese Islamic Cultural Association; more than twenty teachers and staff members from the Islamic Normal School; He Youren, representative of the Islamic Student Magazine; Yang Zhisan, representative of Dunhua Elementary School; Yang Yushu, representative of the Humanitarian Monthly; Da Peisheng, Imam of the Chuanxin Street Mosque; Ha Decheng, Imam of the Zhejiang Road Mosque; Mai Junshan, Imam of the Xiaoshadu Mosque; Ma Shaosheng, Li Yushu, and Ma Yifang, representatives of the Board of Directors of the Xiaoshadu Mosque; Ding Jingan, representative of the Hankou branch of the Chinese Islamic Association; and about a hundred of Mr. Yin's relatives and friends in Shanghai. Mr. Yin checked into the Central Hotel and first went to the Zhejiang Road Mosque for a rest. According to Mr. Yin, he departed from Shanghai in October last year, first passing through Marseille, then arriving in Egypt, where he stayed for three months, before going to Hejaz (a country) to perform the Hajj to Mecca, and then to Jerusalem and other countries to investigate all cultural undertakings. After several months en route, he planned to return to China in June. However, due to the World Islamic Conference in Jerusalem sending representatives to tour and investigate Chinese culture, he was invited to accompany them. Furthermore, because the representatives' passport procedures were delayed, requiring a further three months of waiting, he decided to return to China alone. The various Islamic organizations in this city will hold a welcoming fire gathering next Sunday and invite Mr. Yin to give a public lecture. It is said that he will stay for more than ten days before returning to Taiyuan, Shanxi. (Yesterday's newspaper had a copperplate picture published.)

Playwright Dr. Yu Shangyuan Arrives in Shanghai with Mei Lanfang Yesterday, Mei Discusses Russian Criticism as a New Evaluation of Chinese Opera, Expresses Gratitude for Embassy Support and Allied Reception 126

Mr. Mei Lanfang, the representative of the oriental symbolist school of drama and China's specialist opera performer, and Dr. Yu Shangyuan, professor at Yenching University and drama expert, were invited to perform in Russia this spring. Mr. Mei, together with Dr. Yu, then went to various countries in Central Europe to study theatrical arts, and returned to China from Italy aboard the Italian mail ship "Conte Verde." Yesterday afternoon, the two arrived in Shanghai. The ship docked at the Zhaoshang Bureau North Bund Wharf. Mayor Wu's representatives, Li Dachao, Qian Xinzhi, and Chen Zheqing, Mrs. Mei Lanfang, Fu Zhifang, and more than a hundred relatives and friends from Shanghai came to welcome them. Mr. Mei and Mr. Yu gave separate talks to reporters, discussing their journey in

Welcoming at the dock

The "Conte Verde" mail ship arrived in Shanghai at 2 p.m. It docked at the Zhaoshang North Bund Wharf. Those who went to welcome it yesterday included Mayor Wu's representatives, Li Dachao, Qian Xinzhi, and Chen Zheqing, Du Yuesheng, Zhao Shuyong, Mrs. Mei Lanfang, Fu Zhifang, and more than a hundred relatives and friends. After the ship docked, the welcomers boarded the ship to greet Mr. Mei. Although Mr. Mei was weary from his travels, having been in Russia and Europe for several months, he was still graceful and elegant as ever. Mr. Mei was very busy on the ship, greeting the welcomers

Circumstances of docking

When the ship had not yet docked, Mr. Mei and Dr. Yu Shangyuan stood side by side on the second deck, frequently looking at the shore with binoculars and waving to relatives and friends. When the ship stopped, Mr. Mei received the reporters who came to visit. Although he did not give any concrete talks, he said that he would send a written talk after landing and asked for guidance. He was very concerned about the domestic flood situation, saying that he and Dr. Yu Shangyuan had talked about it during the journey and that after a slight rest in Shanghai, he would respond to the requests of charitable organizations to perform and raise money to help the victims. Both were wearing beige suits, white drill trousers, and white hollowed-out shoes, and were in good spirits. Mr. Mei and Mr. Yu stood talking on the deck for a long time without getting tired. Then, at the request of the photographers from various newspapers, they took a group photo with the welcomers on the deck. In addition, they took a group photo with his wife, Fu Zhifang, and his sons and daughters as a souvenir before leaving the ship. At this time, hundreds of people were welcoming him on the dock, lining the streets to see him, and the traffic was blocked. He returned to his private residence on Rue Massenet at 3 p.m. to rest, while Yu Shangyuan temporarily stayed in a hotel.

Mr. Mei's speech

I was invited by the Soviet Union's External Cultural Association, encouraged by our government authorities, and sponsored by the gentlemen of the Chinese Drama Association. I led the troupe to perform in Russia in February this spring. When I went abroad, I traveled with Ambassador Yan Junren on a special Soviet ship to Vladivostok. The Soviet Union assigned special personnel to take care of us, and the journey was very comfortable. Ms. Hu Die and Mr. Zhou Jianyun, who attended the Soviet Film Exhibition, also happened to be on the same boat, which added to the grandeur. I originally agreed to perform for eight days in Moscow and Leningrad. However, there were still many people who could not get tickets. After repeated requests from the Cultural Association, five more days were added in Leningrad. After returning to Moscow from Leningrad, I performed once again at the Moscow Grand Theatre as a farewell memento. In total, I performed for fifteen days. The TASS news agency reported to the world daily on all the performances at that time, and I heard that the domestic newspapers published them in great detail, so I will not repeat them here. I was very honored to receive unanimous praise from the people of that country and the Soviet dramatic leaders and literary experts for my performance in Russia. The major newspapers in Moscow and Leningrad recorded and commented on it daily, publishing it on the front pages. They mostly commented on the style and techniques of Chinese opera. To summarize the advantages of Chinese opera put forward by the people of that country, there are about three points: (1) Chinese opera includes "singing," "dialogue," "dancing," and "martial arts," which is a mixed art that integrates various skills. (2) The use of color lines on the Chinese stage is most in line with the principles of stage economy without losing its beauty. (3) Every move of a Chinese opera actor has a fixed style, which can be used freely in various scripts, and the actor's performing talent is not bound by this fixed style. The above points are what the Soviet literary and art circles pay special attention to in Chinese opera. However, in my opinion, I dare not make a final judgment on what Chinese opera is. However, taking this opportunity to get sincere comments from the leading figures in the theatrical circles of that country can serve as a reference for a new evaluation of Chinese opera. We were very warmly received by the Soviet Union during our trip to Russia. For example, for all performances, publicity, and receptions, they had detailed organizations, and we also received assistance from the officials of our embassy in Russia, so my colleagues and I felt very convenient. This is not only a personal benefit, but also a manifestation of the friendship between the two peoples. Mr. Ge Gongzhen was always the representative who contacted the Russian side. Mr. Ge has lived in the Soviet Union for a long time and is very familiar with the Soviet culture, so all the arrangements were even more thoughtful, which is heartwarming. As for our performances in the Soviet Union, we relied entirely on the strength of Mr. Zhang Pengchun and Mr. Yu Shangyuan. I should express my deep gratitude on the standpoint of national opera and on personal friendship. As for the dramatic situation in the Soviet Union, it cannot be described in a few words. The government's promotion is strong, and the people's interest is high. Under these circumstances, the Soviet drama is thriving and making rapid progress. According to the latest survey, there are more than 560 theaters in Russia, more than 47,000 actors and practitioners, and nearly 200 drama schools with more than 25,000 students. The future is indeed immeasurable. In addition to performing in the Soviet Union, I went to see plays almost all the time. I visited various theatrical organizations. After the work was done, I went to Poland, Germany, Switzerland, Belgium, England, Italy, and other places to travel, especially paying attention to the theatrical cause. Unfortunately, time was short, and I could not fully learn from them. In short, after visiting and traveling in Russia and Western European countries, I feel that Chinese opera should make special efforts. If Chinese opera is carefully selected and purified, it has its value of preservation and the path of advancement. I passed through Germany and Italy on this trip, and people in those countries hoped that I would lead a troupe to perform there in the short term. The British theater circles and diplomatic circles are particularly eager for this matter and have repeatedly contacted me. However, because of the different languages, texts, customs, and other things in various countries, the arrangement is more troublesome, so it cannot be decided in a short time. I have been with Mr. Xiong Shiyi in London for months. In the past two or three years, various countries have gradually recognized Chinese opera, and the play "Wang Baochuan" written by Mr. Xiong is especially popular. If there is an opportunity for Chinese opera to be performed in the future, it will surely be more welcomed by various countries. Before I went abroad this time, and after I arrived in the Soviet Union, I was deeply grateful for the warm reception given by the Soviet government and the diligent guidance of our embassy. At the opening of my performance in Russia, the Soviet government invited Ambassador Yan Junren to give a speech to the Soviet audience. It is generally recognized in the Soviet Union that this is the first time that a foreign ambassador has given a public speech to the Soviet people, which has greatly enhanced the friendship between the two countries. Ambassador Bao, the Soviet ambassador to China, also happened to be in Moscow at that time and was kindly introduced to me, which I especially appreciate. After arriving in Europe, I also received guidance from our embassies in various European countries, and I was able to study and discuss with theatrical experts from various countries, and I was able to visit theatrical affairs and organizations in various countries. When the ship passed through Singapore on its return voyage, I was greatly welcomed by Consul General Diao and the President of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce, and I also went ashore to visit. When I passed through Shanghai, I was also treated generously by Mr. He Dong and his friends. All of this is what I will always remember in my heart.

Yu Shangyuan's talk

Dr. Yu Shangyuan, professor of art and drama expert, said that this trip to Russia with Mr. Mei Lanfang to perform our Chinese oriental symbolist drama art was well received in Russia. I am deeply grateful. Because Europeans have different understandings of oriental symbolist drama art due to different environments, their views will naturally be different. When we were in Russia, the critics of that country made many criticisms after watching the play, and we sincerely accepted them. When we went to Europe later, we saw the performance of "Wang Baochuan" in England. This kind of script is very well written, but the direction is inappropriate, so it is often inconsistent with the script during the performance. Moreover, Europeans have always valued realistic art, and their views on symbolist art are also different, so we still need to improve the performance of "Wang Baochuan." I will write an article about this trip to Europe to study theatrical arts when I have time to provide reference and research for the national theatrical arts community. I will stay in Shanghai for three or five days and then return to Beiping because the school's semester is about to begin, so I must return to Beiping as soon as possible.

Famous people cleanse the dust

Famous people in Shanghai, Li Shizeng, Qian Xinzhi, and Du Yuesheng, will hold a grand welcome party at the World Society on Avenue Foch tomorrow to cleanse the dust for Mr. Mei. Mr. Mei will also have to go to Beijing to report to the government on his performance in Russia this time. After the matter is completed, he will return to Shanghai. According to Mr. Mei, I received a telegram on the way, about performing to help the disaster relief. I will do my best to ask for help for the victims of the disaster in various provinces, because this is my duty.

Du Yuesheng Takes Office to Mediate Dispute Over Rickshaw Registration, Representatives From Social and Public Affairs Bureaus Once Discussed, French Authorities Said Only Two Points Could Be Considered 128

Xinsheng News Agency reported that the French Concession Public Works Bureau forcibly registered rickshaw pullers without success and continued to detain rickshaws. Rickshaw pullers petitioned the municipal government yesterday, and the social and public affairs bureaus negotiated with the French authorities. Rickshaw merchants asked Du Yuesheng to mediate. The details are recorded below.

Rickshaw pullers petition

Rickshaw pullers, dissatisfied with the Public Works Bureau's registration, sent representatives Xu Hongsheng, Zhou Li, Lü Yigao, Zhou Yongcai, Li Asi, and Yang Yougui to the Municipal Central District to petition the Social Affairs Bureau at 9 a.m. yesterday. Wang Gang, director of the Huigong Section, received them and asked about the rickshaw pullers' situation in detail. The representatives stated their suffering one by one. Wang said that he would convey it to the director and then negotiate with the French Concession authorities. At the same time, they also submitted petitions to the Municipal Government, the French Concession Chinese Association, and the Second Special District Citizens Association for assistance.

Association meeting

The Rickshaw Industry Association held a joint meeting on the evening of the 2nd, with more than 20 people attending. It was chaired by Qiu Chunshan and often discussed: (1) To recommend Qiu Chunshan, Zhang Huaiyang, and Yu Dajin as three representatives to request Du Yuesheng, the Chinese director of the French Concession, to mediate the case. The resolution was passed. (2) The Shanghai West rickshaw merchants joined the Industry Association and established a Shanghai West office. The resolution was passed. (3) The public concession, Zhabei, South City, and Shanghai West rickshaw owners sent letters, willing to be a backing to deal with the case unanimously. The resolution was passed, and letters of thanks were sent.

Du's mediation

After the meeting, the association representatives petitioned Du Yuesheng at 9 p.m. on the 2nd, requesting him to mediate. Du agreed to contact the Public Works Bureau. At 3 p.m. yesterday, Qiu Chunshan, chairman of the Rickshaw Merchants Association, went to Du's residence again to meet with Du Yuesheng and Shang Mujang. The rickshaw merchants' representatives put forward the rickshaw merchants' minimum requirements for this case. Du agreed to try his best to mediate and instructed the rickshaw merchants to wait quietly for a solution. It is said that Du only consulted with the Public Works Bureau.

Authorities negotiate

At 11 a.m. yesterday, Wang Gang from the Social Affairs Bureau and Mr. Li Tongshi from the Public Affairs Bureau talked to the political director of the French Public Works Bureau and the acting police chief of the Public Concession about a solution. The French authorities said: (1) The registration fee is too high and the French consulate will be consulted to consider it. (2) For the vehicles registered in the announcement, from September, the 1,500 vehicles that should be registered in September will be changed to 1,000 vehicles, and the remaining 500 vehicles will be postponed to October for registration, and so on. The other issues will not be considered. The two representatives have informed the association of this intention for consideration.

Indian Tycoon Travels the World to Shanghai, Plans to Stay in China for a Month, to Discuss Revitalizing the Silk Industry 129

The North-China Daily News reported that Indian tycoon and philanthropist Vartan Mal, for the sake of business and health, led his wife and son to travel around the world. He arrived in Shanghai on the Chichibu Maru on Friday and will stay for about five weeks. Mr. Hua is a giant in the Indian silk industry, and his business extends to various parts of the East. He is now a member of the Khatra Hath City Council and is usually charitable. He has repeatedly donated large sums of money to Indian groups in Shanghai and other places. His visit to China aims to investigate the Chinese market and hopes to negotiate a method to increase the number of Chinese silk exports to India and to make Chinese products sell well in the Chinese market. For this reason, he stayed in Hong Kong and Guangzhou for three months and contacted Chinese and foreign merchants about everything. According to Mr. Hua, the US silver policy is a hindrance to commerce in the East, and China is suffering even more. He hopes that the United States will not hold on to this policy for a long time. Mr. Hua also mentioned the fall in the Japanese exchange rate and its impact on Indian trade. After leaving Shanghai, Mr. Hua will go to Japan to stay for two months to investigate the silk market there. Then he will go to the United States, which is his first visit to the United States. Mr. Hua visited Shanghai in 1917. Now he sees new buildings in Shanghai and the Bund area, which is even more magnificent. He was deeply surprised. When he arrived, a large number of Indians went to welcome him.

The Shanghai Times reported that Indian silk merchant Vartan Mal told guests yesterday that the price of Japanese silk is already low, and the Japanese government is subsidizing its exporters, causing the Chinese silk industry to be completely destroyed. The Chinese government should now do what the Japanese government does, subsidize its exporters, exempt silk exports from taxes, and give subsidies to exporters. Otherwise, the Chinese silk export industry will never be revived. Mr. Hua plans to stay in China for a month and will meet with many government officials and business leaders to discuss ways to revitalize the silk industry. When asked if he was sure that Japanese raw silk and silk exporters were subsidized by the government, Mr. Hua replied that without subsidies, the price would not be so cheap. Mr. Hua is on a world trip and set off from Mumbai on February 18 and is expected to return to India in November 1936.

Municipal Finance Bureau Starts Collecting Autumn Property Tax 131

Central News Agency reported that since the Municipal Finance Bureau implemented the method of collecting property taxes in the urban area this summer, the tax households have been enthusiastically paying at the tax collection offices. The bureau issued a notice yesterday that the autumn property tax for this year will be collected from August 1 and will be handled within the prescribed time limit. It is said that the bureau's tax collection offices are now further improving the procedures for collecting property taxes paid by themselves, striving for simplicity. After each tax record is paid, the receipt can be received within two minutes. If an immediate-term check of the Shanghai Bank is used, stating that the Finance Bureau will receive it, and two diagonal lines are drawn on the check, and the words "Collected by the Shanghai Municipal Bank" are written on it, and the post office directly sends it to the respective tax collection office for collection, it will be even simpler for the taxpayers, and it will be convenient for the citizens themselves in three ways: (1) If the words "Collected by the Shanghai Municipal Bank" are written between the two diagonal lines on the check, then the check is transferred to the disaster relief through the Shanghai Municipal Bank collection. Between one collection and one payment, the bank has already proved that the payment has been paid to the Finance Bureau for tax payment. Moreover, after the check is received, the tax collection offices will immediately send or send the property tax bill, so there is no worry that the payment will not be delivered safely. (2) It takes time to go back and forth to pay the tax. If the tax is paid using the above method, the trouble of trekking can be avoided. (3) If the tax is paid according to the above method, even if the check issued is lost on the way, it does not matter, because the check has been drawn with two diagonal lines, that is, it cannot be guaranteed and collected by the bank. Moreover, it is noted in the diagonal lines that it is collected by the Shanghai Municipal Bank, then the check cannot be paid unless it is signed and collected by the bank for transfer and relief. This is a foolproof method, and there is no need to worry about its loss or error. It is also said that when the bureau collected the summer property tax, because there were still a few tax households with more than ten yuan who did not pay the tax within the time limit, the bureau's tax collection offices sent people to collect the tax and charged a fine in accordance with the regulations. Therefore, after the autumn collection is opened this time, it will only take one or two days, and the tax households who pay the tax to the bureau's tax collection offices are more enthusiastic than the previous time, but there is no crowding, so the taxpayers all say it is convenient.

Japanese Merchant's Business Fails, Commits Suicide by Poison in Shanghai 132

The Japanese Shanghai Daily reported that at 11:30 a.m. on the 2nd, a man was found unconscious behind the shrine of the Shanghai Shrine on Jiangwan Road. The shrine priest Tsurude suspected that he was a patient and immediately reported it to the Dixwell Road Police Station of the Public Works Bureau. The police sent him to Fumin Hospital. The diagnosis result was suicide by poison. It was found that the man was Ogihara Kunio, 38 years old, from Gunma Prefecture, Japan. He arrived in Shanghai on the Shanghai Maru on July 29 and stayed at the Dongguan on Seward Road. He had only two yuan in his purse and a suicide note addressed to the Japanese Consul General, which roughly stated: "In recent years, I have been engaged in the silk business. Due to the social depression and the government's control, the industry has suffered failure. I have no choice but to commit suicide." After emergency treatment by Fumin Medical, there is no danger to his life. At the same time, the police station of the Consulate General specially sent staff to conduct a detailed interrogation and consider the aftermath.

Great Change in Ethics, Brother Kills His Brother, Forcing Him to Borrow Seven Yuan, Chops Him to Death, Disposes of the Body to Eliminate Traces 133

A Jiangbei stone boat, Public Works Bureau registration number 33995, owned by Gao Liqiao, 38 years old, from Funing, with a younger brother named Gao Liya (born to different mothers by the same father), 22 years old, who was by nature addicted to gambling and spent money without restraint. He had previously borrowed seven yuan from his brother Liqiao. On the day before, Liqiao asked Liya to return the seven yuan because the food in the boat was exhausted, in order to buy rice. As a result, a conflict occurred, and Liya was indeed chopped on the head by his brother with a sharp axe and died instantly. He disposed of the body in the Yuncao Creek in order to eliminate traces. This happened at 1 a.m. on the day before (2nd). Because it was late at night, no one noticed it. It was not until 1 p.m. that Chen Weisi (31 years old) and Gao Changheng (44 years old, both from Funing), crew members of the boat, secretly reported to the Wu Song Water Patrol Fourth Detachment of the Public Security Bureau, Captain Jiang Fuyuan. Captain Jiang heard the report. Because it was a serious murder case, he immediately sent Police Chief Zhang Kefeng, Police Officer Zhou Jiakun, Wu Jinyou and others to the boat to arrest the murderer Gao Liqiao, the deceased's wife Gao Wangshi (22 years old), and the crew member Gao Libiao (Sun and Tang cousins, 28 years old), and found a sharp axe, the murder weapon, and a cotton quilt stained with red blood, and took them all to the detachment. After Captain Jiang's interrogation, Gao Liqiao confessed that he asked his brother for seven yuan to buy rice. But Liya not only refused to return it, but also quarreled unreasonably and wanted to chop me with an axe. So I snatched the axe and chopped back, and chopped his head to death. The rest of his words were vague. Captain Jiang inquired about the cause of the incident. Because it was a murder case, he specially prepared a document and sent the police to send the murderer Gao Liqiao, his dead wife Gao Wangshi, and five men and women to the Shanghai Water Patrol General Team. After this incident, the boat gangs generally discussed that Gao Liqiao and his brother's wife Wangshi were suspected of adultery and murder, etc. However, whether it is true must be proved after the court's investigation. The body was found at the bridge pier of Yuncao Creek at 9 a.m. yesterday and was dragged to the Water Patrol Fourth Detachment. At the same time, it was reported to the local court to send someone to Song to examine it.

Yesterday morning, around five o'clock, he took an axe and went to the shoe shop to find his rival. He found Yang sleeping soundly and, unable to contain his anger, he struck Yang's head twice with the axe, inflicting fatal injuries. Blood gushed out, and Yang was on the verge of death. Seeing the enormity of his crime, the assailant fled. His colleagues discovered the attack and reported it to the Yinxiang Township Police Station. The police chief sent an inspector with officers to arrest the perpetrator, but he had already vanished. China Travel Service Organizes Tours, Providing Travel Opportunities for All Sectors and Benefits for Members 136

Since its establishment, China Travel Service has been dedicated to serving travelers and has earned a distinguished reputation. In recent years, with the expansion of its business, it has established branches and hostels in major cities across the country, striving to benefit travelers in every possible way. The company has recently organized tour groups, widely recruiting members, with a far-reaching purpose. Details are as follows:

Tour Group Objectives: The company believes that travel is a noble form of entertainment that can enhance knowledge and strengthen the body. In Europe and America, people of all social classes have the opportunity to travel. However, in China, due to the underdeveloped transportation and relatively high costs of transportation and accommodation, the pleasure of travel is mostly enjoyed by the middle and upper classes, while ordinary people are often constrained by their financial resources. The company believes that to address this shortcoming, it is necessary to organize tour groups for group travel, using the most economical methods to enable ordinary people to enjoy the pleasures of travel. The company will carefully plan all aspects of transportation, accommodation, and meals to minimize costs while striving to ensure comfort and enjoyment.

Tour Group Regulations: Name: The group is named the China Travel Service Tour Group. Objectives: The group aims to promote famous scenic spots and historical sites, encourage group travel, enhance interest in travel, conduct on-site inspections, strengthen the body, and broaden horizons. Membership: Anyone who supports the group's objectives and is willing to abide by the group's rules can join as a member. Categories: There are four types of members: honorary members, permanent members, special members, and ordinary members. Fees: Honorary members are appointed by the company. Permanent members pay a one-time fee of 50 yuan in national currency and are not required to pay any further fees. Special members pay an annual fee of 20 yuan in national currency. Those who pay for three consecutive years are also considered permanent members and are not required to pay any further fees. Ordinary members pay an annual fee of 5 yuan in national currency. Benefits: All members are entitled to the following benefits: (1) Members will receive travel magazines on a regular basis. (2) Members will receive a 10% discount when staying at the company's hostels or hotels by presenting their membership card. (3) Members will receive a 30% discount on all publications purchased from the company at the list price. (4) Members will be notified of tour schedules and travel news at any time. (5) Members will receive a set of exquisite calendars at the end of the year, with the tour dates for the year marked, worth two yuan. (6) Members can attend lectures to exchange travel knowledge and broaden their horizons. Branches: All branches of China Travel Service in major cities in China have branches of this group. Registration: Registration can be made at the head office of China Travel Service at No. 420 Sichuan Road, Shanghai, from today onwards, or inquiries can be made at the branches in other cities. Welcome to join.

Travel Details: (1) All travel itineraries, accommodation, and meals for the tour will be planned and prepared by China Travel Service. Upon departure, the company will send staff to accompany the tour and take care of everything. (2) The dates, locations, and travel expenses for long-distance tours will be published on the exquisite calendar provided. Other short-distance tours will be planned and determined by China Travel Service and notified to the members. (3) When departing for a trip, all members must strictly adhere to the notified time and gathering place. (4) Members wishing to join a trip must register in advance with their membership card and pay the full travel fee. The group will issue a temporary receipt, which will be exchanged for a formal travel voucher upon gathering for departure. (5) If a member has registered and paid the fee but does not participate in the trip, the member will be responsible for the losses incurred by the group due to the member's cancellation, and the remaining amount will be refunded. (6) Non-members who wish to temporarily join a group tour must be introduced by one or more members of the group and complete the membership procedures in order to enjoy the same benefits. This restriction does not apply to members' families (parents, spouses). (7) For group travel, it is essential to adhere to the schedule. Losses incurred due to individual delays will be borne by the individuals themselves. (8) The meals and accommodation for members during the travel period will be pre-determined by China Travel Service. If a member desires extra comfort and wishes to pay extra for separate meals and accommodation, they may do so, but the fees paid will not be refunded. (9) Members who submit travel notes, scenic photographs, etc., to travel magazines will be given appropriate remuneration if they are accepted and published. (10) If members propose to travel to a certain place and the proposal is signed by more than ten members, or if it is proposed by a member and the group gathers more than ten members, the trip will be organized. (11) Addenda: (a) Members should wear the group badge on their left lapel during travel for easy identification. (b) Members should take care of their personal belongings to prevent loss. Large items can be entrusted to China Travel Service for safekeeping. (c) Members should respect public morality and maintain order when departing. (d) During the travel period, members should obey the instructions of the leader.

This Year's Plans: The company will organize tour groups several times each year. Long-distance tours, such as to South China, North China, Northwest China, and Sichuan, will be organized about three or four times. Short-distance tours will be organized at any time depending on the climate and environment, approximately dozens of times each year. A long-distance tour will be held as soon as the autumn weather cools down and is currently being planned.
