Shengjing Steamer Raises Anchor, Unearthing Nameless Female Corpse Amidst Waves, Underbody Lacking Trousers, Seeming Severely Beaten, Diamond Ring, Watch, and Cash Found on Body 137

Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, while the Swire Company's steamer "Shengjing" was raising anchor at the French Company's Pier No. 1 for departure, the water churned due to the paddle wheels' movement, and a nameless female corpse suddenly surfaced. The lower body was naked, the skin was not severely discolored, and the facial features were still very clear, suggesting death not long ago. Chinese Constable Duo, No. 42 of the Customs Water Police Station, retrieved the body. The detective chief of the police station's criminal division, suspecting foul play, examined the body on a sampan. The upper body was clad in a white voile short shirt over a striped calico shirt, but there were no trousers. The feet wore gray thread stockings and black serge shoes. The hair was in a bun. The deceased appeared to be about 27 or 28 years old, wearing a blue gemstone-inlaid earring in each ear and a gold-mounted diamond ring on the ring finger of her right hand, also wearing a gold watch. Sixteen five-yuan banknotes from the Bank of Communications, one five-yuan banknote from the Industrial Bank, three ten-yuan banknotes from the Industrial Bank, one one-yuan banknote from the Silver Industry Bank, three one-yuan banknotes from the Bank of Communications and Commerce, two one-yuan banknotes from the Bank of China, three twenty-cent coins, two ten-cent coins, and sixteen cents in small foreign currency were found in her waist pocket, indicating considerable wealth. A cursory examination of the body revealed slight swelling, but there was redness on the buttocks, suggesting severe beating. Other than that, there were no obvious injuries. The cause of death was suspected to be murder. However, the gold jewelry and cash were not taken, which presented an interesting puzzle. Since the body was discovered near the French Concession, the detective chief felt a joint investigation was necessary and notified the French Concession police station in the evening, requesting them to send personnel to investigate and handle the case. The water police dispatched detectives to investigate thoroughly that night. The body was sent to the Salvation Bureau morgue for examination, and the local court was notified for further inspection.

Manufacturing Red Pills Causes Feud, Fellow Apprentice Commits Murder, Feng Muqing Treated at Hospital, Qian Shanhai Arrested Upon Return to Shanghai 138

Feng Muqing, a thirty-year-old local resident of No. 130, Liu Lane, Makchi Road, Julaiqi Road, French Concession, and Qian Shanhai, an eighteen-year-old local resident from Longhua, Xixiang, were originally distant relatives and fellow apprentices. Their elders, both surnamed Gu, considered them brothers. Feng and Qian were partners in manufacturing red pills, which led to a feud and animosity between them. On the morning of June 18th this year at 6:30 AM, Qian Shanhai gathered five or six fellow gang members, armed with axes, and stormed Feng's house. While a maid was emptying a chamber pot, Qian and the others rushed in, went straight to Feng's bedroom, and, without any explanation, attacked Feng, who was still asleep in bed, striking his legs twelve times with the axes. They also left a threatening letter before fleeing. The threatening letter stated that the attack was a warning, and that if the police were notified, they would return to take Feng's life. To avoid further trouble, Feng Muqing did not report the incident to the police and sought treatment at the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road. On the 28th of last month, Feng received another threatening letter while in the hospital. The hospital authorities, upon discovering this, reported it to the French police, who dispatched Detective Bu Zhenglong to inquire about the incident and begin investigating the assailant. It was discovered that Qian Shanhai had returned to Shanghai and was hiding in Room 12 of the Haitong Inn at No. 11, Lane 15, Yunnan Road, Public Concession. At 1:00 AM on the 2nd, in conjunction with the Laozha Police Station, detectives went to the Haitong Inn and arrested Qian, bringing him back to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo presided over the hearing. Fei Xizhen, a lawyer from the Police Department, presented the case, stating that the defendant was arrested for attempted murder and that the Police Department had not yet completed its investigation. He requested a postponement to apprehend the accomplices and investigate the case thoroughly before formally prosecuting. Detective Bu Zhenglong then reported the details of the arrest. Qian Shanhai confessed that he had not committed murder, but had fought with Feng Muqing along with five others. He said that he was often treated poorly by Feng, so he went to injure him. He claimed that the others who went with him also had grievances against Feng. The detective also reported that the victim was recovering well in the hospital and would be discharged soon. After reviewing the confession, the court ordered a postponement of the hearing to August 13th and ordered the defendant to be detained.

Rabid Dog Causes Tragic Death of Bitten Woman 139

Ji Zhang, a thirty-nine-year-old woman from Yiting Township, earned a living by farming. Her husband was blind and stayed at home all day. Last month, while Ms. Ji was working in the fields, she was bitten in the leg by a rabid dog. Despite seeking treatment everywhere, the results were minimal. Her condition worsened, and local doctors were helpless. On the day before yesterday, she pleaded with her neighbor, Tong Hengchun, to accompany her to Shanghai for medical treatment. However, upon arriving at Dafang Lane near Xiaobeimen, Ms. Ji suddenly went mad, flailing her arms and legs and becoming mentally incoherent. Tong Hengchun was startled and tried to stop her, but she collapsed and rolled on the ground, dying shortly thereafter. The local police took Tong to the Laobeimen Police Station for questioning. Yesterday morning, they ordered Jiang Banyuang, the local head of the Ninth Ward, to report the incident to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Ouyang Shu, accompanied by a forensic examiner, arrived at the scene, confirmed the death, and ordered Tong Hengchun to arrange for burial as soon as possible.

Jiang Jinmu Severely Injured by Six Axes Due to Feud Over Teahouse Girl, Police Arrest Two Culprits 140

Jiang Jinmu, a twenty-seven-year-old carpenter from Ningbo residing at No. 158, Pushi Road, French Concession, and his wife, Jiang Wang, a thirty-year-old woman also from Ningbo, worked as a domestic helper. Recently, Jiang frequented the Tianyun Amusement Park on the roof of Wing On Company, where he had an affair with a teahouse girl. This was discovered by a rival, and a feud developed. Around 7:00 PM on the 2nd of this month, Jiang was sitting alone outside No. 158, Pushi Road, cooling off when a group of over ten thugs, armed with axes, attacked him without explanation, striking his body all over. Amidst the commotion, Jiang was struck over ten times in the head and waist, and fled. The assailants chased after him until patrolling Chinese constables No. 49 and No. 58 from the French Police Station arrived, helped to arrest Wang Haixi (27 years old), a native of Songjiang, and seized two axes from his hands. Mu Shiheng (28 years old), a native of Shandong, was also arrested as a suspect. The others scattered and fled. The police sent the injured Jiang to Guangci Hospital for treatment. His injuries were severe and life-threatening. Yesterday morning, the police escorted the suspects to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District, where Judge Zhang Qianzuo presided over the hearing. Fei Xizhen, a lawyer from the Police Department, stated that the defendants were arrested for attempted murder and that the Police Department had not yet completed its investigation, requesting a postponement to apprehend the accomplices and investigate the case further. The detective stated that the suspect had been struck with six axes and that his injuries were severe and life-threatening. He requested that a medical examiner be dispatched to Guangci Hospital to examine the injuries. Detective Lu Dongliang then reported the details of the incident and presented the two axes as evidence. Defendant Wang Haixi confessed that he was summoned by Sun Fugen from Liu Jixiang Road near Xieqiao at 4:00 PM the previous day, who gave him an axe and instructed him to commit the attack due to a dispute over a teahouse girl at Wing On Company. Mu Baoheng claimed that he lived at No. 178, Pushi Road, and was accidentally bumped into by the injured man, causing bloodstains on his shirt, but he denied participating in the attack. Constables No. 45 and No. 58 testified that they saw the victim fleeing with the first defendant chasing after him with an axe, so they arrested him. After reviewing the confessions, the court ordered a postponement of the hearing to August 8th and ordered the defendants to be detained. The two axes were temporarily stored in the evidence room.

Zhejiang Local Bank Inspection Report 144

The 66th Inspection Report of the Zhejiang Local Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states that the committee members and commissioned accountants, in accordance with the committee's rules, inspected the Zhejiang Local Bank's issuance reserve fund. The 66th inspection was conducted at the bank on July 31, 1935, and the results are as follows: Total amount of banknotes issued: 1,936,250.50 yuan, including: Silver dollar notes: 2,475,805.70 yuan, Subsidiary currency notes: 460,444.80 yuan. Total amount of banknote reserve fund: 2,926,250.50 yuan, including: Cash reserve in silver dollars: 1,991,090.05 yuan, Security reserve converted to silver dollars: 944,160 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Zhejiang Local Bank's banknote regulations, 60% of the banknotes issued must be backed by cash reserve and 40% by security reserve. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve is above 60% and the security reserve is below 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. July 31, 1935. Special Announcement

Reading Supplementary Statistical Materials of Shanghai Municipality Compiled in the 23rd Year of the Republic (1934) 148

— Huang Huopei

Following the Shanghai Municipal Local Association's compilation and printing of the "Shanghai Municipality Statistics" in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), it compiled and printed supplementary materials in the 23rd year, following the previous compilation. It still covers areas like land, population, administration, judiciary, finance, banking, commerce, industry, labor, transportation, public utilities, cultural affairs, education, society, and health. However, the agriculture section is temporarily omitted because a field survey was just conducted, and only a year has passed. Most of the materials are supplemented up to the 22nd year, with some supplemented up to the 23rd year.

The total value of real estate transactions in Shanghai was 84.52 million yuan in the 19th year of the Republic (1930) (originally silver taels converted at a 1.4 discount, the same below), 183.4 million yuan in the 20th year (1931), 24.85 million yuan in the 21st year (1932), and 43.09 million yuan in the 22nd year (1933). The 22nd year was only slightly better than the year of the "January 28th Incident" (1932) in Shanghai. Compared to the most prosperous year, the 20th year, it was less than a quarter. The total construction value of the city in the 22nd year was only over 72 million yuan. Compared to the most prosperous year, the 19th year, with 110 million yuan (silver taels converted at a 0.4 discount), it was less than three-quarters.

The city's population, however, increased. In the 19th year, it was 3,144,805 people. In the 20th year, it increased to 3,307,432 people. In the 21st year, it decreased to 3,133,712 people. In the 22nd year, it increased again to 3,223,8628 people.

There were a total of 110,675 school-age children in Shanghai, of which 55,836 were enrolled in school, accounting for 50.44%.

The total operating expenditure of the Shanghai Municipal Government's medical institutions under various bureaus in the 17th year (1928) was 4,146,538 yuan, and the income was 4,834,991 yuan. In the 18th year (1929), the operating expenditure was 5,345,196 yuan, and the income was 5,866,092 yuan. In the 19th year, the operating expenditure was 6,344,734 yuan, and the income was 7,310,985 yuan. In the 20th year, the operating expenditure was 6,998,215 yuan, and the income was 7,737,284 yuan. In the 21st year, the expenditure is unknown, but the income was 8,789,984 yuan. Both income and expenditure increased every year. The Shanghai International Settlement's Municipal Council's regular expenditure in the 21st year was 16,465,291 taels, and the income was 15,169,553 taels, with income insufficient to cover expenditure. In the 22nd year, the regular expenditure was 17,125,657 taels, and the income was 15,800,983 taels, with income also insufficient to cover expenditure. The French Concession's Municipal Council's regular expenditure in the 21st year was 5,680,698 taels, and the income was 6,038,521 taels. In the same year, the temporary expenditure was 1,021,815 taels, and the income was 3,528,400 taels, with income exceeding expenditure.

In the 21st year, the Jianghai Customs imported over 54.02 million taels of silver and exported over 29.2 million taels, indicating that imports were still greater than exports. In the 22nd year, imports were over 75.75 million taels and exports were over 85.15 million taels, indicating that exports were greater than imports.

In the 21st year, the Jianghai Customs' import value was over 755.16 million yuan, and the export value was over 246.66 million yuan. In the 22nd year, imports were over 736.21 million yuan, and exports were over 315.75 million yuan. In the 23rd year, imports were over 600.48 million yuan, and exports were over 271.3 million yuan. Exports were less than imports, with a difference of two to three times.

Among the important imported commodities, cotton, rice, wheat, flour, paper, and cotton cloth all decreased year by year. For tobacco and machinery, the total value in the 23rd year was lower than the average price in the 21st year, but slightly higher than in the 22nd year. The import value of steel, wood, kerosene, and gasoline was highest in the 22nd year.

Among the important exported commodities, tea and beans were the only categories with gradually increasing value each year. From the 21st to the 23rd year, tea increased from over 28.19 million yuan to over 30.32 million yuan. Beans increased from over 2.69 million yuan to over 4.4 million yuan. Leather also showed improvement. Eggs decreased year by year. The most disheartening was silk, which went from over 44.94 million yuan in the 21st year to over 4.25 million yuan in the 22nd year, and then plummeted to over 24.79 million yuan in the 23rd year.

Shanghai's wholesale price index was 112.4 in the 21st year and 103.4 in the 22nd year.

Shanghai had 61 silk filatures with over 15,000 reeling machines in the 22nd year. Compared to 112 factories with over 25,000 reeling machines in the 21st year, the decrease was almost half.

Taking the 15th year of the Republic (1926) as the base of 100%, the Shanghai workers' cost of living index in the 21st year for clothing, food, housing, fuel, and miscellaneous items was 108.05%. The purchasing power of silver dollars was 92.55%. In the 22nd year, the total index was 97.17%, and the purchasing power of silver dollars was 102.91%.

Shanghai's total postal statistics showed that there were over 19,597,000 letters in the 21st year, which increased sharply to over 32,785,000 letters in the 22nd year.

The number of public and private schools at all levels in Shanghai in the 22nd academic year was 967, with 185,661 students and over 12.86 million yuan in funding. Compared to the 20th academic year, all aspects showed progress.

Shanghai's statistics on suicides showed that there were a total of 1,946 suicides (male and female) in the 22nd year. Those who committed suicide due to quarrels were the most numerous, totaling 787, accounting for 40.44%. Family problems were next, with 406 people, accounting for 2.086%. Economic oppression was third, with 389 people, accounting for 20%. This was 570 more people than in the 21st year.

Shanghai's statistics on divorces showed that there were 503 cases in the 22nd year. Among them, incompatibility was the most common reason, with 452 cases, accounting for 89.86%. This was 88 more cases than in the 21st year.

In the 22nd year, there were 256 robbery cases in Shanghai, 29 more than in the 21st year. There were 18 kidnapping cases, 3 fewer than in the 21st year.

There were 126 assassination cases in Shanghai in the 22nd year, 26 more than in the 21st year.

Shanghai's death rate per thousand people in the 22nd year was 8.65%, slightly higher than in the 21st year, but significantly lower than in other years. The death rate per thousand Chinese residents in the International Settlement was 17.6% in the 21st year, slightly higher than before. In the 22nd year, it was 12.8%, significantly lower than before.

The source of the materials used in this book is noted at the end of the table, as in the previous edition. Although the above listed items only offer a glimpse, a slight examination of the economic situation is sufficient to indicate that Shanghai's economic downturn has reached a serious level. Furthermore, the increasing population reflects the bankruptcy of the rural areas in the interior. Reflecting on the past and thinking about the future, one cannot help but feel deeply concerned.

Police in the International Settlement Solve Robbery Case in Three Hours; Robbers Steal Over a Hundred Watches to Divide the Loot Somewhere; Two Robbers Arrested While Pawning Watches 149

Li Yongchang Clock Shop at 477 Fuzhou Road was suddenly broken into by four robbers at 7:10 PM the night before. Two robbers pulled out handguns and threatened those present, stealing 480 yuan in cash and 135 watches of various types, worth over 1,800 yuan in total, and fled with the loot. Afterwards, the shop owner reported to the police and requested an investigation. The police notified all precincts to be on the lookout. Unexpectedly, in less than three hours, the case was solved by Detective Shang Wu and Investigator Shen Dehui of the Police in the International Settlement. After the robbery, the thieves went somewhere to divide the loot. Two of the robbers, Fan Shengliang and Zhang Afu, hid five of the stolen watches and took them to Lifeng Pawnshop at 271 Kaifeng Road around 10 PM the night before to pawn them for cash. They were spotted by Detective Shang and others, who suspected their behavior and arrested Fan and Zhang. They seized five watches and four pawn tickets and took them to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Qian Xunjiu presented the case, saying that because the time was too short, a detailed investigation could not be carried out, and requested permission to detain them. Judge Wu Zehan questioned the two defendants and allowed them to be detained for further review in seven days.

Shanghai Tennis Club Organizes Open Singles Tournament 152

Divided into Groups A, B, and C

The Shanghai Tennis Club's open singles tournament passed the regulations through the club committee yesterday. Because the tennis players participating in the National Games arrived in Shanghai late, the registration deadline for Group A singles has been extended to August 28th, and the competition will start on September 1st. However, the registration deadline for Group B and C singles will be at 12:00 noon on August 15th, and the competition will start on Saturday, August 17th. Those who aspire to win the championship silver cup donated by Nanyang Tobacco Company should join as soon as possible. Registration fees are accepted by mail and can be contacted at the Shanghai Tennis Club on Kangdi Road (telephone 82387) or Mr. Chen Qihao at Xiangmao Foreign Firm on Guangdong Road. The regulations are recorded as follows:

(1) This competition is limited to Chinese citizens, who must pay a membership fee. Group A is 4 yuan per person, Group B is 3 yuan per person, and Group C is 3 yuan per person. The court will be provided by the club (members of the club will receive a 1 yuan discount from the original membership fee).

(2) Registration dates for Groups B and C are from August 5th to August 15th. The deadline for Group A is August 28th.

(3) Players are divided into Groups A, B, and C, based on their tennis skills. The club will determine their level based on their past performance. Once the level is determined, if a player has an objection, they must submit a written statement with reasons, and the committee will re-determine it. The committee's decision is final and cannot be changed.

(4) The competition order will be arranged by the club. The competition period for Group A is from September 1st to the end of September. The competition period for Group B is from August 17th to September 15th. The competition period for Group C is from August 15th to September 15th.

(5) Players must specify the date of participation when registering, which will be arranged by the club. Absence once will be considered a forfeiture (if both players agree to reschedule, they are free to do so, but the court used after the deadline must be approved by the club, otherwise they must find another court).

(6) The club will donate a silver cup for each group champion on behalf of Nanyang Tobacco Company. A silver cup will also be awarded to each group runner-up as a souvenir.

(7) Players participating in the competition must bear the cost of three "Slazenger" new balls for 1935 (Editor's note: This shows a lack of industrial and commercial revitalization. Players must pay a registration fee of four yuan or three yuan each, so the balls used for the competition should be provided by the club. At the very least, the two players in the match should share the cost of the balls used).

(8) The competition rules are based on the regulations of the British Lawn Tennis Association, and the trust referee system is adopted. Referees will be invited to supervise the finals.

(9) In the event of a protest, a formal protest letter must be submitted to the Honorary Secretary's Office within 24 hours after the incident for the committee to review. The committee's decision is final and cannot be protested. A protest deposit of 5 yuan must be paid for each protest. If the protest is valid, it will be refunded afterwards; otherwise, it will be confiscated.

(10) Matters not covered in these rules may be amended by the club at any time.

Education News

Announcement from the Ministry of Education: Standards for One-Year Short-Term Courses 155

The Ministry issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 3rd, stating: "Regarding the Provisional Regulations for One-Year Short-Term Elementary Schools, orders have previously been issued to be followed. Now, based on Article 9 of the Provisional Regulations, the Provisional Curriculum Standards for One-Year Short-Term Elementary Schools have been formulated. In addition to being publicly announced, these Provisional Curriculum Standards, a copy enclosed, are hereby issued to be followed and further instructed to be followed by all relevant parties. This order."

Provisional Curriculum Standards for One-Year Short-Term Elementary Schools

1. Explanation: (1) This curriculum takes the national language (content including general knowledge, and assignments being reading and writing) and arithmetic (including mental arithmetic, abacus, and written calculation) as the foundation, supplemented by civic training and recess exercises (including singing and games). (2) This curriculum is specifically designed for children aged nine to twelve (inclusive) for one year. (3) When implementing this curriculum, emphasis should be placed on utilizing local facts or materials to aid children's understanding. 2. Objectives: (1) Instill civic morality and cultivate essential moral habits for citizens. (2) Teach basic hygiene knowledge and cultivate essential hygiene habits for life. (3) Teach basic knowledge of the country's history, geography, and civics, enabling them to understand the relationship between individuals and society and the nation, and cultivate a sound national consciousness. (4) Teach basic knowledge of the natural world, enabling them to understand the relationship between the natural world and human daily life. (5) Enable them to recognize approximately 1,400 characters and be able to read simple vernacular texts. (6) Enable them to write practical vernacular texts for daily use, such as letters and diaries. (7) Enable them to use phonetic symbols to read simple vernacular texts and, to the extent possible, be able to understand and speak the national language, aiming to achieve language unification. 3. Time Allocation:

Subject　Weekly Class Periods　Minutes per Class　Total Weekly Class Minutes

National Language　12　45　540

Composition　2　30　60

Writing　4　30　120

Arithmetic　6　30　180

Civics　6　15　90

Training　6　15　90

Recess Exercises　6　15　90

(Explanation) (1) For a half-day, two-shift system, divide the children into morning and afternoon classes. The number of class periods and time are the same for both morning and afternoon. (2) For a full-day, two-shift system, divide the children into two classes, attending school full-day. The two classes teach each other, and the number of periods and time are the same as in the table above. However, when one class is in session, the other class should simultaneously have self-study or extracurricular assignments. (3) For a mixed full-day and half-day two-shift system, divide the children into two classes, one class attending school full-day, and the other class attending school half-day (morning or afternoon). The teaching time for the full-day class must be matched with the half-day class, morning and afternoon. However, when the half-day class is in session, the full-day class should simultaneously have self-study or extracurricular assignments. (4) National Language Curriculum Content: Regarding compilation, (1) Regarding compilation, 1. Evenly distribute and arrange important materials from history, geography, civics, nature, and hygiene, without using fairy tales, stories, or myths. 2. Reading of practical daily texts: notes, letters, cards, announcements, diaries. 3. Reading of simple explanatory and narrative texts. 4. Practice in checking dictionaries. 5. Recognition of common punctuation marks. 6. Recognition and application of phonetic symbols. 7. Practice in listening and speaking the national language. (2) Regarding materials: A. History: 1. Admirable words and deeds of famous people and great achievements of past dynasties, focusing on inspiring national self-confidence and self-respect. 2. Modern national conditions and reforms, focusing on national consciousness and the conditions for creating a modern nation. 3. Mr. Sun Yat-sen and the National Revolution, focusing on Mr. Sun Yat-sen's dedication to the National Revolution. B. Geography: 1. A general overview of our country's terrain, mountains, rivers, climate, products, transportation, and administrative regions, focusing on our country's unique natural advantages and an outline of the General Plan for National Reconstruction to inspire thoughts of cherishing the country and material construction. 2. Our country's capital and important cities, focusing on the relationship between cities and rural areas, making them aware of the importance of rural construction. 3. Ceded territories, concessions, extraterritoriality, foreign ships navigating inland rivers, and the transfer of railway and mining rights, explaining the loss of national rights and making them aware of the significance of self-strengthening and wiping out humiliation. 4. Recognition of the Earth's shape, oceans, continents, and the location of our country and important countries in the world, focusing on the relationship between the great powers and our country, making them aware of our country's position in the international community and the importance of national defense. C. Nature: 1. Changes in the four seasons and their relationship with living things. 2. Clouds, rain, frost, dew, ice, snow, sleet, wind direction, temperature, humidity, etc. 3. The effects of lightning and methods of avoiding it. 4. The causes of solar eclipses, lunar eclipses, rainbows, solar and lunar halos, meteors, comets, earthquakes, volcanoes, etc., and the debunking of superstitions. 5. The harm of mosquitoes and other pests and methods of eliminating them. 6. The relationship between beneficial and harmful insects and crops. 7. Explanation of essential daily necessities: clothing, food, housing, transportation. 8. Promoting land reclamation, focusing on afforestation. 9. Explanation of major agricultural products. 10. Prevention of floods, droughts, and fires. D. Hygiene: 1. The structure, function, and health care of the human body's external form. 2. The structure, function, and health care of the human body's internal organs. 3. The harm of addictions such as smoking and alcohol. 4. Prevention and first aid for infectious diseases. 5. Public hygiene. (5) Composition Curriculum Content: 1. Sentence construction practice. 2. Practice in practical texts such as notes and letters. 3. Application of common punctuation marks. (6) Writing Curriculum Content: 1. Writing practice of recognized characters. 2. Writing practice of practical texts. 3. Recognition of the most commonly used cursive script. (7) Arithmetic Curriculum Content (Mixed teaching of written and abacus calculation): 1. Recognition of numbers and writing of numerals. 2. Addition and subtraction. 3. The multiplication table and division formulas. 4. Multiplication with factors of one to three digits. 5. Division with factors of one to two digits. 6. Application of four operations. 7. Four operations with decimals. 8. Conversion of our country's weights and measures and currency. 9. Bookkeeping and accounting methods. 10. Practice in mental arithmetic and abacus calculation. (8) Civic Training: 1. Cultivation of cleanliness, strength, vitality, and various hygiene habits. 2. Training in various virtues such as honesty, fairness, quickness, initiative, discipline, responsibility, mutual aid, and courage. 3. Cultivation of various habits such as labor, production, thrift, and saving. 4. Training in political awareness such as public service, law-abiding, patriotism, and love for the group. (9) Recess Exercises and Singing Games (Textbooks to be compiled separately): 1. Indoor recess exercises. 2. Outdoor recess exercises, singing and games. 4. Local games. 5. Competitions (such as rope skipping, shuttlecock kicking, etc.). 6. Posture training.

Ministry of Education Announces Measures for Short-Term Vocational Training Classes

The Ministry of Education recently announced the "Provisional Measures for Short-Term Vocational Training Classes" through a ministerial order. The articles are as follows: (1) Short-term vocational training classes aim to train technical personnel for specific industries. All kinds of training schools, training institutes, lecture halls, etc., that cultivate technical personnel belong to this category. (2) The standards for running short-term vocational training classes are as follows: (1) Senior vocational schools and specialized schools may establish them if they recognize a social need for technical personnel. (2) Administrative agencies may establish them if they need technical personnel within their administrative scope or entrust schools to run them. (3) Private individuals or organizations may run them if society or their established enterprises need certain types of technical personnel. (3) The training period for short-term vocational training classes is set from three to fifteen months, depending on the nature of the profession. (4) Short-term vocational training classes are temporarily divided into the following two types: 1. Recruiting those with a junior high school education or equivalent and providing them with a suitable period of training. 2. Recruiting those with a senior high school education or equivalent and providing them with a suitable period of training. (5) The curriculum of short-term vocational training classes focuses on specialized technical subjects. Completion of certain subjects constitutes completion of the program. (6) When establishing a short-term vocational training class, detailed plans for the establishment of subjects, curriculum, equipment, funding, etc., as well as teacher qualifications and student fees, must be submitted to the competent educational administrative authority for approval and record-keeping. (7) The establishment of public short-term vocational training classes should be investigated and reported by the provincial and municipal educational administrative authorities to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping. The establishment of private short-term vocational training classes should be reported by the establishers to the local competent educational administrative authority and forwarded to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping. (8) When short-term vocational training classes begin classes, the roster of teachers and students, as well as the entrance examination scores, should be reported to the competent educational administrative authority for record-keeping. (9) At the end of each term of short-term vocational training classes, the roster of graduating students, academic performance, and implementation overview should be reported to the competent educational administrative authority for record-keeping. (10) Students in short-term vocational training classes who pass the examination after completing the training period may be issued a certificate of academic achievement in a certain technical subject.

Municipal Education Bureau Issues Order Prohibiting Student Petitions

Requests to administrative agencies must no longer use students as tools

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to the city's private primary and secondary schools, stating: "In accordance with Municipal Government Order No. 14782, regarding Zhiren Elementary School leading young students by its person in charge on a long journey to petition the government regarding school building rental issues, regardless of the truth of the request, such actions of using students as tools are highly inappropriate and should be prohibited by the Bureau to emphasize education." In view of the foregoing, student petitions are akin to coercion and damage academic pursuits, which is highly inappropriate. In accordance with the aforementioned order, all schools are hereby ordered to refrain from using students as tools to petition in the future when making requests to administrative agencies, and instead submit written requests. This is an important order that must be strictly followed.

Improvement Plan for Zhengfeng Middle School

Zhengfeng Middle School in this city has a history of over ten years since its founding. At the beginning of this summer vacation, the former Principal Huang resigned from both his positions as school director and principal because he was serving in the Jiangsu Surveillance Commissioner's Office and could not attend to school affairs. After deliberation at the school's third board of directors meeting, his resignation was approved, and school director Wu Kaixian was elected as chairman, and school director Hu Changzhi succeeded as principal. It is known that Mr. Hu is an educational expert in our country with profound knowledge and experience. Since taking over, he has made many improvements in school affairs. Yesterday, Principal Hu also published an outline of the school affairs improvement plan he drafted, adding the following:

First, Regarding Material Construction: Shanghai is an area where Chinese and foreign cultures converge, with frequent transportation and a gathering of talent. Young people studying here can cultivate flexible hands and brains, and can observe and feel the path to progress. However, the poor air quality and extravagant living of the residents are its major drawbacks. The school's location is near Xujiahui, adjacent to the National Chiao Tung University's School of Taxation, which is both quiet and convenient for transportation. Judging from the above-mentioned advantages and disadvantages, all points occupy a good position. However, the limited school buildings restrict development. The school has now determined its budget and will first requisition vacant land in the vicinity of more than twenty acres in area during this year, using one-half for sports grounds, and building a tuberculosis sanatorium and a trachoma student isolation room for students to exercise and strengthen their bodies. The remaining vacant land will be used to build a Zhengfeng Library, which will move the existing school library into it, and add 5,000 new books, with a reading room attached to assist students in extracurricular study. This project will be completed in about three or four months and will be available for use in the twenty-fifth year. After the start of the first semester of the twenty-fifth year, two three-story student dormitories and a three-story teaching and office building will be built on the remaining land, which is expected to be completed in six months. By the start of the second semester, the existing school buildings can be completely moved in. Even if the number of students increases in the future, there will be room for expansion.

Second, Regarding Psychological Construction: Spirit is the skeleton of a career, and psychology is the direction of action. Therefore, in addition to material construction, the school is also committed to psychological construction. Tracing back to the last hundred years, the Chinese nation has suffered from the invasion of foreign forces, and has been frustrated and defeated, and it is almost impossible to end the day. Secondary schools are an important stage in the educational process, and this cannot be ignored. The school's future plan is to have all teachers set an example and cultivate a spirit of hard work, endurance, courage, and progress, with a clear understanding of their abilities in everything they encounter, so they will not retreat, and with the ambition to do good, so they will not lag behind. However, the cultivation of this kind of academic spirit depends on the usual training, and it is determined that it cannot be achieved overnight. The most important aspect of training is excellent teachers, otherwise, the example will not be established and inspiration will be difficult to generate. Therefore, starting from the next semester, the school plans to follow this policy and invite famous teachers to take teaching positions, adhering to the educational principles of the Three Principles of the People, and providing beneficial guidance to students in all aspects of their lives as much as possible. Each grade will have a homeroom teacher under the direction of the Dean of Student Affairs, organizing a student life guidance committee to live and study with students, setting an example for students at all times and in all places. Over time, the effect of imperceptible influence can be achieved. In addition, the formulation of teaching affairs, curriculum progress, increasing experimental work, limiting student leave, and holding strict examinations are all discussed in the principal's improvement plan, but because the matters involve trivialities, they are not fully recorded here.

Little Boy (4) 156

— Original by American author Louisa May Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

"Have you seen Aunt Shu yet?" he asked, as if this were an important courtesy.

"I haven't seen anyone except you children; I'm waiting," Ned replied. "Did Uncle Lao send you here?" Xiaoqiao continued in a gentle and solemn tone.

"Mr. Lao sent me here."

"He is Uncle Lao; he always sends good children here."

Upon hearing this comment, Ned couldn't help but show a pleased and satisfied expression on his face, and smiled slightly, making his thin face seem very lovely. He didn't know what else to say, so the two looked at each other in silent agreement, until a little girl ran over with her doll. She looked a lot like Xiaoqiao, but not as tall, and had a redder, rounder face and a pair of blue eyes.

"This is my younger sister, named Xiaomei," Xiaoqiao said, as if introducing a rare and precious treasure.

The children nodded to each other: the little girl's face seemed to be full of joy, deeply showing two dimples, and then she said with affection:

"I hope you can stay. We have so much fun here; don't we, Xiaoqiao?"

"Of course, that's why Aunt Shu came to Meizhuang."

"This really seems like a very good place," Ned also joined in his opinion, feeling that he couldn't help but say a few words in front of these two amiable young people.

"This is the best place in the world; isn't it, Xiaoqiao?" Xiaomei said, she clearly considered her brother the most knowledgeable.

"No, I think Greenland, with its icebergs and sea lions, is even more interesting than here. But I also love Meizhuang, it is indeed a good place, and it's good to be able to live here," Xiaoqiao replied, he was at that time reading a book about Greenland. (Note 5) He was about to open that book to show Ned some of the illustrations and add some explanations, when suddenly the maid came back, nodded towards the door of the guest room, and said, "Okay; you can stay here."

"I'm so happy; let's go see Aunt Shu now." Xiaomei said, and took one of Ned's hands, looking like she was protecting him, which was so lovely that it immediately dispelled all of Ned's fear of unfamiliarity and loneliness.

How to be a True Athlete (In All Seriousness) 157

— Xiangming

Children, have you seen those athletes? They have strong bodies, solid muscles, and faces exuding heroism, stepping with powerful strides; everywhere showing their heroic spirit. Children, are you envious?

However, how can one become a true athlete? Just go to exercise often after class, and practice whichever kind you like. But don't neglect your proper studies, just like building a house, if you lay a good foundation, then building it layer by layer will not be too difficult.

Casual Chats on Children's Anecdotes (Stories) 158

— Yisheng

Fan Xuan Loves His Body

When Fan Xuan was eight years old, he was picking vegetables in the backyard and accidentally injured his finger. He couldn't help but cry loudly. Someone asked him, "Is it because it hurts?" "No, it's only because I remembered that the book says, 'Our body, hair, and skin are received from our parents, and we dare not injure or damage them,' so I cried!" he replied.

Everyone's body is passed down from their parents and should serve society and the community. Everyone should protect their body and not injure it. The sentence quoted by Fan Xuan comes from the Classic of Filial Piety, which teaches people to value self-love as part of filial piety. In an extraordinary state, he was still able to remember the education he received from books, which is worthy of our respect and emulation.

Kong Rong's Eloquence

When Kong Rong was young, he sought an audience with a high-ranking official named Li. The official Li had a high position, and because there were too many guests visiting every day, he was unable to receive them all, so he instructed the gatekeeper that only relatives and old friends could be reported. Kong Rong had already heard of this practice, so he told the gatekeeper that he and the master's family had been friends for generations, and only then was he able to achieve his goal of meeting. Li Huan asked him, "You say that we have been friends for generations?" He immediately replied, "Isn't it so? Don't you remember the friendship between my family's sage and your family's Laozi?" The host was praising him to the skies when a guest sitting nearby interjected, "He's clever when he's young, but he may not be good when he's older!" Kong Rong turned around and replied, "I suppose you, sir, were definitely clever when you were young." The guest was immediately speechless.

There is a folk saying in Jiangnan, "Three years old determines eight years old, eight years old determines a lifetime." This means that observing a person's words and actions in their youth can reveal their entire life. Kong Rong's agile eloquence was a gift from heaven and could not be forcibly learned through human effort. Ultimately, he became a famous official and Confucian scholar in the late Han Dynasty, which shows that the folk saying is correct.

Etiquette for Social Conversation (Civic Training) 160

— Kang Jianzhai Husband

If one is not born mute, then speaking is a right endowed to us by nature.

Impetuous people, upon meeting strangers and exchanging brief greetings, launch into lengthy, detailed conversations. Those who are inarticulate, however, become timid upon meeting strangers and can't utter a single word. Both of these attitudes are somewhat inappropriate.

"Nature gave us two ears but only one mouth."

"No matter how foolish you are, people won't realize it if you don't open your mouth." These sayings are meant to warn people to be careful about what they say. On the other hand, "Only conversation can dispel a dull atmosphere; only conversation can bridge the gaps between us; and only conversation can harmonize estranged feelings."

When meeting a stranger for the first time, conversation must be calm and unhurried. Don't be impatient or quick-tongued. Speaking loudly, making grand pronouncements, and constantly chattering with those sitting near you without regard for others are all flaws that should be avoided.

"You're wrong!" "I don't think so." "Outrageous!" "Humph!" (exhaling through the nostrils) These impolite tones should be carefully avoided.

"Please forgive me." "I'm sorry." "I think that..." These humble tones can be used often.

When the other person is speaking animatedly, don't interrupt them.

When the other person shows signs of fatigue, don't bore them with endless chatter.

If the conversation isn't engaging, there's no need to talk much.

When angry or upset, try to restrain yourself from speaking.

When asking someone a question, adopt a humble attitude, saying "Excuse me..."

When someone asks you a question, answer them clearly, concisely, and logically.

Sweet Sugar (Crafts) 161

— Zhen

Children's Year has begun! Min'er gathered the neighborhood children to hold a small music gathering to celebrate this happy Children's Year.

Min'er's father specially bought many candies to distribute to them. As soon as Min'er saw the candy, he took a lot for himself. His older brother, Cong'er, scolded him:

"Younger brother, you really don't know etiquette. You didn't distribute some to the neighborhood children first, but took so much for yourself. Weren't you complaining about a toothache yesterday?"

"Brother, yes, but sugar can help with digestion, so I want to eat more. It's fragrant and sweet, a win-win. Wouldn't it be silly not to eat it?" Min'er said, mumbling with sugar in his mouth.

"Eating a little can help with digestion; eating too much will cause stomach acid to build up, slowing down digestion. If sugar decomposes in your mouth, it will damage your teeth, which is why you often have toothaches."

"Didn't Mom say that rock sugar can cure coughs? Then I'll eat rock sugar."

"Rock sugar is still sugar, just a bit more refined. Eating too much is still not good."

"Oh! I won't eat too much sugar, but I don't know how it's made?"

"Sugar is made from sugarcane and beets. In our country, sugarcane is mostly used. In the morning, it's cut down, the skin is peeled off, and it's pressed in a stone roller. The squeezed juice is boiled in an iron pot, and the impurities that float to the top are gradually skimmed off. Lime is added, and after one or two hours, it's taken out and filtered through cloth. Then it's evaporated over a low flame until the juice is thick. It's placed in a cold pot and stirred constantly with a stick. When it's cooled to the right time, it's poured into a clay pot to crystallize, becoming brown sugar. Removing the molasses from brown sugar can make white sugar. Dissolving white sugar in water to make a concentrated liquid and placing it in a jar will gradually solidify into a semi-transparent solid, which is rock sugar."

"Sugarcane, can it be cultivated here?"

"Not here. Sugarcane likes to grow in warm places, so Guangdong and Fujian produce a lot."

"What kinds of sugarcane do we commonly see?"

"There are two kinds: the green-skinned one is called bamboo cane, and the red-skinned one is called Kunlun cane."

Soft Water and Hard Water (Common Sense) 162

— Zhang Yuqing

Children! Mr. Nature may have already told you? Water has ground water and underground water distinctions. What I'm going to talk about here is that soft water is ground water; hard water is underground water. Now, let's briefly analyze it like this:

Summer is a season that makes people sweat. Therefore, handkerchiefs and towels have become our daily necessities, but sometimes they slowly turn black and stiff; but some places handkerchiefs and towels, even when worn out, are still white and soft. This is not a relationship between sweat and handkerchief quality but a water problem. Also, some copper teapots, although used for a long time, are still very clean; some places will form a thick layer of dirt. This is also not related to the long-term use of copper. It is also a water problem. Furthermore: some places water can moisturize people's skin: but some places water will make people's skin rough. This is also a relationship between water. In short, anything that makes towels handkerchiefs turn black and harden; causes dirt on copper teapots! Causes rough skin are all related to water, and it is hard water rather than soft water.

Any water that does not contain mineral impurities is called soft water; water that contains such impurities is called hard water. Because this kind of impurity, if it undergoes a chemical reaction with other substances, other things will be harmed by it.

(1) Nitric acid, sulfuric acid, etc. contained in hard water erode soft cotton fabrics (such as handkerchiefs and towels), and their softness is reduced because of the deprivation of moisture, and they become black and hard because they absorb other mineral impurities.

(2) After hard water is boiled by fire, some mineral impurities will precipitate, causing dirt to accumulate, and at the same time, because the evaporated acid enters the essence, it is very easy to make it rot.

(3) Hard water erodes people's skin, then the fat will combine with the acid, which can make the skin rough.

Needless to say, well water and spring water flow underground, so they naturally contain more mineral impurities, so they are often hard water. Some of the tap water in Shanghai is also groundwater (like artesian wells), which must undergo extremely fine filtration and chemical processes to remove its hardness. However, some private artesian wells have simple equipment due to economic problems, so there is even more hard water, which we should pay attention to.

How to Correct Bad Reading Habits? (Talk) 164

— Linghu Zhao

Dear children, there are several bad reading habits. You usually overlook them when you are reading. Now I would like to bring them up and talk about them, hoping that you will all correct them.

The first bad habit is that you think you understand it a little bit, and that's it. This is not a big loss for general knowledge of Chinese, but it won't work for arithmetic! Because if you don't understand arithmetic from the beginning, you will become more and more confused later on! So when you are taking the exam, you are dumbfounded and can't do it, that is so sad!

The second bad habit is greed. You look at this book and flip through that book. As a result, you spend a lot of precious time and don't finish reading any of them.

The third bad habit is that you have no perseverance. You read when you are happy, and when you are not happy, you just play. How can you improve your reading then?

Children, to correct the first bad habit, you must first prepare a notebook, write down the unclear words and sentences, and ask your classmates or teachers. You must understand it before you stop! For the second bad habit, we must first pick a book and not flip through another book until we have finished reading this one. There is also the third bad habit: we must set a self-study schedule and develop the habit of reading regularly every day. This will not only solve the difficulties of exams, but also increase your interest in reading and gain advanced knowledge and learning.

Okay, I hope you children will work hard to correct your bad habits.

Summer Toys (Handicraft) 165

— Xu Baozhang

Children! In addition to studying, we should also use our hands to create something! Not only does it feel very interesting, but it also shows our children's intelligence and wisdom. Wasn't the convenient transportation of steamboats and trains invented because Watt invented the lifting of kettle lids when he was a child? Wasn't the omnipotent electricity invented because Franklin invented flying kites when he was a child, and then one invention after another? Children, let's invent!

These days are the hot summer months. It is very interesting for our children to sit in the courtyard to enjoy the cool air, tell stories and jokes, and guess riddles. But, wouldn't it be even more interesting if our children could make a few more toys to play with?

(1) Watermelon Lantern　Take a round watermelon and scoop out the inside , everyone eats to cool off in summer. Draw some flowers and birds on the melon skin, write some words, and slowly carve away the green skin according to the traces of the calligraphy and painting. Insert a small nail at the bottom of the melon for lighting a candle. Tie ropes on the four corners and hang it in the courtyard. When the candle is lit at night, the flowers and birds look lifelike from a distance, and the green light shines in all directions, isn't it very beautiful? If you imitate the method of making a carousel lantern, draw five or six shadow figures and attach them to the bottom of the paper wheel, pass an axis through the wheel and insert it into the melon. Once the candle is lit, the air next to the paper wheel moves due to heat, and cold air comes to fill the gap, creating wind that drives the paper wheel to spin. From a distance, the characters move as if they are alive, much like watching a movie, which is even more interesting.

(2) Lotus Lantern　Use bamboo strips to tie a lotus lantern and paste it with paper of red, green, yellow, white and other colors. Light a small candle inside. Or use clam shells, store vegetable oil and lamp wick in the middle, light it up and place it in the pond. Floating up and down, like countless twinkling stars, embellishing the water beautifully, it is very beautiful.

In addition, fold transparent paper into a firefly cage and catch a few fireflies and put them inside. The firefly light shines out, and it is also a good toy. After the summer month passes, a cool breeze slowly comes, and the autumn insects of Qu Qu Ji Ji are produced in time. This is a very happy season for us. Cricket cages, bell cricket cages, and grasshopper cages are also toys that children can make themselves.

Children's Year Aspirations 166

— Heart Green

On this day, the breeze was gentle and the sun was bright. Although it was summer, it didn’t feel hot, just like the late spring weather when orioles fly and grasses grow. It was about six o'clock in the evening, and the setting sun gradually cast its rays on a small garden in the city. In the garden, two tall sycamore trees were golden as if coated with a layer of gold. Under the trees, on a patch of grass, several children sat in a circle. In front of them were many cakes, candies, paintings, calligraphy, and toys. They were talking, laughing, and very happy. It turned out that they were holding a celebratory gathering to mark the opening of Children's Year.

One of the older children stood up and said, "Everyone, Children's Year has begun! This year is of great significance to us children, and we must not let it pass lightly. Today's gathering should also be something meaningful. We can't just eat, play, talk, and laugh and think that's enough."

Immediately, everyone said in unison, "That's right, that's right, we should do something meaningful, but how are we going to do it? You are the chairman today, so please give us your opinion."

The chairman lowered his head and thought for a moment, then opened his mouth again and said, "Our teachers at school have said well: 'Everyone has aspirations. Everyone should set their aspirations when they are children, so that when they grow up, they can proceed according to their aspirations.' So, I thought that taking advantage of the opening day of Children's Year, everyone could talk about their future aspirations."

The children unanimously raised their hands and said, "Agreed! Agreed! But who should speak first?"

The chairman said, "Let's go in order of the number of strokes in our surnames, starting with the one with the fewest strokes."

So, a child surnamed Ding stood up and said, "My surname is Ding, with only two strokes, so let me speak first: My father is a comprador in a foreign firm. He earns thousands of dollars a month, wears Western suits every day, eats fancy meals, lives in a Western-style house, and rides in a car. Look how comfortable he is! So, when I grow up, I also want to be like my father and become a comprador in a foreign firm."

Next, a child surnamed Wang stood up and said, "My surname is Wang, with only four strokes, so let me speak second: My uncle is a great lawyer. He is very famous and earns a lot of money. Even though he doesn't work as a comprador in a foreign firm, he still lives in a Western-style house and rides in a car, so I want to be a great lawyer in the future."

Next, a child surnamed Bao stood up and said, "My surname is Bao, with only five strokes, so let me speak third: My uncle is a county magistrate. He manages a county of hundreds of miles, and the local people call him 'County Lord.' He is in charge of everything in the area. His status is high, and his income is also high. I think being an official is better than anything else, so I want to be an official in the future."

Next, a child surnamed Ren stood up and said, "What's so rare about being a county magistrate? Being a military officer is better than being a civil official. Don't you see my uncle? He is a division commander in the army, with tens of thousands of soldiers under his command. Whether it's the battalion commander, regiment commander, or brigade commander, they all have to listen to his orders. How imposing that is! So, my aspiration is to be a division commander in the future."

Next, a child surnamed Li stood up and said, "Your aspirations are not my aspirations. At school, I like Chinese and drawing the most. My grades are always above ninety points every semester. According to my father, if I study hard, I can become a writer and artist in the future. As long as I have the skills, I can still earn a lot of money. Besides, my reputation will be great, and my status will be high, so I have already decided on my aspiration."

Next, a child surnamed Hu stood up and said, "My aspiration is the highest. It's completely different from yours. What do you think it is? It turns out that I want to be an aviator. In the future, I can sit in an airplane and fly high in the sky, flying, flying, flying, and going wherever I want freely. How interesting that is! In case of war with other countries, I can also contribute to the country."

Finally, the chairman smiled, stood up, and said, "My surname is Chen, with the most strokes, so I have to be at the end. I dare not agree with any of your aspirations except for being an aviator. Since the beginning of this semester, after listening to the speeches of several teachers, I have aspired to science, because science can save the country. You must know that China is so poor and so weak because science is not developed. Science is very broad. Let's start with diligent study of zoology and botany. When we enter middle school, we will focus on physics and chemistry, and study step by step. In the future, it will be very useful. I plan to make a career in science. First, I want to invent some new items that are beneficial to the public, and then open mines to extract raw materials and open factories to manufacture them cheaply. Although this aspiration is great, I must strive to do it. I hope you will all strive to do the same and aspire to be scientists."

Commercial News: Central Bank Gold Bar Rates Announced; Gold Speculation Resurges

Outside the Market, it Once Broke the 900 Yuan Mark, Repeatedly Rising to 917 Yuan, Further Setting a New Increase of 10 Yuan and 6 Fen

The gold market was initially sluggish yesterday but then picked up, and the speculative trend showed no signs of stopping. Reports of economic experts' discussions had a slight impact on the market. However, due to an economic intelligence report from Shen Shi News Agency, which contained buying advice, some people anticipated buying opportunities. When the Central Bank announced the official rates, the upward trend began, breaking the 910 yuan mark and rising to 917 yuan several times. The strength of bullish sentiment was evident. Initially, overseas silver markets in the UK and US were stable, and Montevideo forward silver prices were unchanged or slightly lower (less than 1%).
