Women's World

Occasional Thoughts on the Opening of Children's Year 173

— Jenny

On the eve of the long-publicized Children's Year, just before the grand opening ceremony was held across the country, newspapers reported that a Xu surname elementary school teacher in Ji County, suffering from lung disease, bought a child from a poor family and cooked him alive. This seems to deliberately unveil Children's Year, telling how desolate and cruel it is behind this colorful and brilliant curtain! It is already common for innocent children to be abandoned, sold, or killed along with their poor parents. As long as we are not forgetful, we can still recall the tragic events not long ago when parents took their children and "jumped from high buildings" and "swallowed raw opium" to commit suicide. Therefore, when implementing Children's Year, instead of designing more for wealthy children, it is better to pay more attention to the poor children who are displaced or struggling on the hunger line. The widespread establishment of labor nurseries, infant care centers, and educational institutions are all urgent matters. This will not only benefit the majority of future masters of the country, but also reduce a burden for women struggling on the death line, opening a line of life.

The Polygamous Life of the Powerful and Influential 174

— Shun

Recently, newspapers have reported a piece of news that has attracted our attention, that is, the escape of Tang Yulin's wife from her family. This matter is very common, but it happened in a powerful and influential family, so it gives the general public a particularly deep impression.

Regarding Tang Yulin's wife's appeal, it seems that it has not yet aroused public opinion. Such a shameless thing has happened in a powerful family, and the impact will be unimaginable. Standing in the position of women, we should have the right to comment. From the perspective of correcting social customs, it is also necessary to evaluate right and wrong to warn future generations.

According to the Great American Evening Post on July 25, Tang Yulin's first wife, Tang Liu, left home and went to Tianjin due to Tang's abuse, and entrusted lawyer Bao Yang to negotiate with Tang. According to the statement, the reasons for her leaving home are: "Mr. Tang specializes in favoritism and is naturally rude and violent. It has long been taken for granted that he whips and abuses within the boudoir. Under this violence, she only knows how to be submissive and strive for perfection. She originally wanted to grow old together, but the concubines surrounded her and spent their days fighting. Mr. Tang, bewitched by them, treated her cruelly (I don't want to list the facts, and I can't bear to list the facts). He is truly inhumane. Twenty years of cohabitation, if it were not for the weeping pleas of my daughter, my life would almost not have been saved. Thinking of this, my flesh trembles and my heart is terrified. Recently, he has become more and more abusive to my mother and daughter, like a nail in his eye, he must remove it. The malicious abandonment has been very obvious. In such a bad environment where I am not safe from morning to evening, it is really difficult to live together again. Therefore, I took my daughter and escaped empty-handed to Tianjin. For the sake of my life safety, there is no reason to return and re-enter the snare."

In this statement, we can see three points that are beneficial to women.

First, Tang Yulin relied on his power to widely acquire concubines and treat women as playthings.

Second, Tang Yulin relied on his power to "whip and abuse" and "cruelly" treat his first wife, with whom he had lived for twenty years. He is truly inhumane.

Third, Tang Yulin was the former chairman of Rehe Province. As the dignity of a provincial governor, he actually lived a polygamous life and whipped his first wife. If this trend continues, the upper ranks will emulate the lower ranks, and women across the country will share the same fate as Tang Liu.

People say that the army is always brave in internal wars and timid against foreign enemies. This is indeed true. Tang was originally a warlord. When he invaded Rehe, Tang claimed that the righteous army did not listen to orders and abandoned their armor and fled. This is his attitude towards foreign enemies. Now he is accused of abusing his first wife. The internal affairs of the family are exposed. This is Tang who can neither defend against foreign enemies nor appease his family. Thus, the original form of the warlord is completely exposed!

In short, Tang Yulin, who is in the position of the head of a province, owns a group of concubines and abuses his first wife, which is a heinous crime, but for the sake of the future of women, we must carry out severe criticism and merciless attacks!

Women's Issues Forum

Section Six: Illegitimate Children and Their Mothers 175

— Jun Hui

In capitalist society, lifelong monogamy is the ideal of law and morality, while promiscuous polygamy is the common reality and practice. It is quite open and common for a man to have concubines, maids, mistresses, and even prostitutes, indulging in licentiousness. Neither the laws of the country nor the moral opinions of society blame him, and he himself does not feel that this is immoral behavior. However, if a woman has a secret affair with another man besides her legal husband, it is a heinous crime. The law will immediately arrest her, and social opinion will condemn her as an unchaste and promiscuous woman, determining her lifelong fate. This is the "sacred" monogamy of capitalist society, both inside and out.

However, this unreasonable system inevitably produces unreasonable results. This result is the illegitimate child, considered the "crystallization of sin" by civil society. The laws of capitalist countries regard all life born outside the bounds of monogamy as the fruit of sin, branding it with the stigma of illegitimacy, depriving it of its civil rights, and abandoning it outside the protection of the law. But it is not only the illegitimate child who is sacrificed here, but also the illegitimate child's mother, who is seen as a "demon of sin." She is despised by people and her life's happiness is ended. On the other hand, the man's legal wife is also a victim of love. This point must be noted.

The mothers of illegitimate children are mostly underage, poor women and fallen, bankrupt middle-class women. To survive in a social relationship where gold is in the hands of men, they often fall into the trap of love through male seduction, deception, and coercion, which is no different from entering the eighteenth level of hell, with no hope of return. Their children and themselves have to live in darkness, unseen by the light of day. When they think of this, they resolutely resort to desperate acts—suicide, infanticide, abortion, etc., but what public opinion gives them is still the name of sin. Yet they are unwilling to find the root of her sin in this social system!

In order to strictly maintain the glory of monogamy, the civil class subjects hundreds of thousands of illegitimate children to the "sin of being born," depriving them of their civil rights. The Napoleonic Code of France prohibits illegitimate children from recognizing their fathers. Article 1589 of the German Civil Code "does not recognize the kinship between illegitimate children and their fathers." In particular, the law of Argentina stipulates: "Children born of incest or adultery shall not have fathers or mothers, and it is forbidden to recognize their fathers and mothers. Neither father nor mother may even recognize them as children."

Until the World War, the above principles became immovable truths in the family laws of various countries. However, the French law of November 16, 1912, made an exceptional amendment, that is, "Except in cases of rape and seduction, in cases of enticement, de facto cohabitation, and when the father recognizes his children, the father-child relationship is recognized."

Then, why do capitalist countries want to deprive illegitimate children of their "right to life"? The court scholar Meisel most frankly stated this reason, saying:

"It is not in the interest of the state to give children born of licentiousness the same fate as children born legitimately. Why? Because if this were the case, the motive for formal marriage would be eliminated... Also, it is not in the interest of the state to give the same happiness to those without married life as to those with married life. Why? Because the state of family is more beneficial to the country and more helpful to the country than the state of free single people."

This is the entire philosophy of civil society on this issue, and the main reason why the state abandons countless innocent lives of illegitimate children.

As a result of society depriving illegitimate children of their right to life, their mortality rate is twice that of legitimate children. According to a German survey in 1920, the mortality rate per hundred births was 11.9 for legitimate children and 23.0 for illegitimate children. According to Schulte's survey, one in seven legitimate infants died, while one in four illegitimate infants died. According to the same survey, most of the mothers of illegitimate children belong to the working class. For example, among the 94,777 illegitimate children born in Prussia in 1906, 42% were domestic servants, 10% were agricultural laborers, and 22% were industrial laborers.

Many biologists collect evidence of various biological, moral, and intellectual defects in illegitimate children to prove the fact that illegitimate children lack human value. But some scholars among them with a scientific conscience also admit the superior talent and value of illegitimate children. Otto Neurath, the greatest educator in modern Germany, argued:

"Among illegitimate children, there are indeed physical and mental degenerates. But this phenomenon is no more common than in legitimate children. Moreover, the vitality of illegitimate children is often superior to that of legitimate children. Why? Because most illegitimate children are born from genuine love relationships, and are born when their parents are as beautiful as flowers."

Although the laws of capitalist countries use various methods to prevent the inevitable process of illegitimate births, the number of those born is increasing day by day. According to Kuczynski's investigation, the number of illegitimate children in Germany has increased by 40% in the past five years, and there are now 2.5 million illegitimate children. This exposes a major hole in the modern monogamous system. Someone said: "In modern society, there is no such thing as marriage." This statement is by no means without reason!

The Marriage Life of the Miao People in Guangxi 176

— Luo Qiong

The Miao and Yao people live in seclusion in the deep mountains of Guangxi. Due to inconvenient transportation, they are still in a stage of "not interacting with each other until death." Therefore, various customs and habits cannot be communicated with each other, and there is a phenomenon of "different customs every five li, different customs every ten li." Marriage customs are certainly no exception. The following introduction is limited to the situation of some Miao people in the Miao Mountains of northern Guangxi. Before explaining the marriage customs, I would like to first describe the social interaction between men and women. Young men and women there are not bound by the "no physical contact between men and women" rule. As long as they know each other, men can chat and sing all night at the women's houses, freely indulging in a sweet love life. This is the "sitting with a girl" that is common among the Miao people.

After a considerable period, when both parties believe they can get engaged, the man proposes to his parents to ask a matchmaker to propose marriage to the woman's family. As long as the woman's parents agree, the engagement is decided on in a verbal contract between the two parties. From then on, during each solar term or busy farming season, the man's family can bring the woman over, and even the woman's sisters often accompany her to help with work, such as carrying firewood, cooking, and other farming or housework. However, the duration of their stay can only be single nights, such as three nights, five nights, etc. This situation continues regularly until the marriage.

After two or three years, the marriage life begins. Their marriage period is mostly around the third or fourth day of the new year. Before the marriage, the man's family must prepare one or two dan or three or four dan of glutinous rice, ducks, fish, firecrackers, and one or two taels (equivalent to one dollar and sixty cents in small foreign currency) of silver as a gift for the wedding party. The woman's dowry is also equally simple, requiring only a set of cotton bedding, two boxes, and a weaving machine and a spinning wheel each. Sometimes, cows are also given as dowry, which probably depends on the economic situation of each family, but the difference is very small. One or two days or three to five days before the wedding, the matchmaker brings the woman to the man's house. When departing, the bride, escorted by three or four female companions, carrying one liter and three handfuls of white rice, quietly leaves her mother's house at midnight and does not enter the husband's house until four or five o'clock in the morning. At this time, the groom must hide outside, and the family members also remain silent. With the help of the matchmaker and female companions, a grand wedding ceremony is held. The wedding ceremony is as follows: next to the stove, sour fish, sour meat, and duck wine are placed. The bride, the matchmaker, and the female companions all sit around the stove and sincerely worship the gods. After this act is completed, the matchmaker takes all the wine and dishes and feeds them to the bride one by one in a solemn manner.

On the big day of the wedding, which is also what the Miao people call the "wedding day," the man's family takes the gifts prepared before the wedding, accompanied by seven or nine men, and sends the bride and groom back to the woman's house. Along the way, the companions sing and play music, laughing to their heart's content. When they arrive near the woman's village, there are one or twenty people who also sing and play music to welcome them. At the same time, there is also a mountain sedan chair prepared for the groom or his companions to sit in. After sitting in the sedan chair, three to five yuan in small coins must be prepared as a thank-you gift. On the way to the woman's house, various sheds made of bamboo sticks or firewood are erected everywhere to express welcome. Once they arrive at the woman's house, the woman's family entertains them well. That night, the man's wedding party and the woman's relatives and elders have a feast together, singing and answering each other, and toasting each other. The sound of joy is deafening. They do not disperse until they know that the east is turning white.

After the marriage, the woman still lives at her mother's house. During her stay, the woman's chastity is not a concern, so she often secretly conceives a child, who is considered her husband's child. She only returns to her husband's house for a few days during the solar terms and busy farming season. It is not until after she has a child that she lives with her husband regularly. Therefore, the woman's dowry is not sent to her husband's house until after she has had a child. The entire marriage process is then concluded.

Draft completed on July 24, 1935

Medium-Length Fiction

Returning Home 177

— Su Hong

"Lend it to me temporarily, perhaps a letter from their (referring to her sons) father will arrive soon, and I will definitely return it to you by the end of the year."

"I think you'd better borrow from someone else... Aju! Work faster! See, you get lazy when I talk to others."

The sister-in-law turned around helplessly and slowly came to the child's side, sitting down to breastfeed the child.

Madam Wang put on a stern face and muttered to herself in a low voice:

"Coming to borrow rice from me, where do I get so much rice? Really, always coming to me..."

The sister-in-law pricked up her ears to listen, secretly shedding tears.

Xiu Zhen stood up, thin as a donkey, as if at a loss for what to do. The sister-in-law looked at her, showing a disgusted expression:

"Sister! Come and take a look at these two little devils for me. Originally, you haven't been home for a few days, and I shouldn't ask you to do anything, but really, your sister-in-law is having a hard time, one person doesn't have enough time to do so many things." She was about to leave this place to go to the great-grandfather at the back of the house, but it happened that the great-grandfather had just strolled over from the back. Although the great-grandfather was old, he was still healthy. Now, he no longer needed to personally handle field work and mountain work, having entrusted them to his three sons, and even more so, a group of hired farmers honestly worked for him all day long. However, he would still do small things, sometimes weaving straw sandals, sometimes binding brooms.

The great-grandfather greeted Madam Wang, as he was here to ask Master Wang to buy southern goods. Master Wang was the manager of a certain southern goods store in Ningbo, and asking him to buy would give him a discount. The great-grandfather was just about to explain his intentions to Madam Wang when the sister-in-law stopped him and said:

"Great-grandfather! I was just about to go to your place, I want to discuss something with you." Her voice lowered again. "Lend me another two jin of rice, their father will probably have a letter soon, and I will definitely pay you back by the end of the year."

"Borrow rice! I'm having difficulties myself, I painstakingly planted a few acres of fields, but they were all scorched to death by the sun. The harvest is bad, but the land tax is still high. Even if I have a few grains of rice, it's not enough for me to eat myself."

"Great-grandfather! Just lend it to me, I will definitely pay you back by the end of the year. We don't have any rice to cook today, and we can't fill our stomachs with just this ice-cold mustard greens." She pointed to a small vegetable garden in front of her.

"You want two sheng of rice?" The great-grandfather looked at the small garden. "You've already borrowed one dou from me before; hmm... I see... I'll give you another two dou of rice..."

"That's great, that's great! Thank you, great-grandfather, you will always be blessed, you are so kind!"

"But... you mortgage this vegetable garden to me."

"Mortgage the vegetable garden to you?" The sister-in-law hesitated, thinking that this vegetable garden was the source of vegetables all year round. With this vegetable garden, she wouldn't have to buy other vegetables, and she could get by just buying some salt and soy sauce. Her mind turned over and over. "Great-grandfather! Lend me two sheng of rice first, let me think about this matter."

"If you don't mortgage it, it's up to you, but don't borrow from me. I said long ago that I don't have much rice. Even if you mortgage it to me, those two dou of rice will have to be ground from the grain. But having a little more rice is worth it, even if it changes hands."

The sister-in-law went to ask a few neighbors, but still couldn't get any rice. Noon had already arrived, and the children were crying for food. The sister-in-law thought that if her husband still had no news, then the problem wasn't just a matter of one or two meals, how would they get through the year? She panicked for a while and decided to mortgage the vegetable garden to the great-grandfather. She ran to the great-grandfather's place:

"Great-grandfather! I think you should give me three dou of rice, that way I can eat until the new year."

"How about I give you two and a half dou?"

"Then! Great-grandfather! Two dou and eight sheng, I won't say any more."

The sister-in-law invited a schoolteacher to write the contract, and the inkstone and brush were already borrowed. When the schoolteacher wrote the date, he asked:

"From what day?"

"Naturally, from today," said the great-grandfather.

The sister-in-law said hurriedly:

"Great-grandfather! From the fifteenth day of the first lunar month next year! Wait until the mustard greens grow."

"You said from the fifteenth day of the first lunar month next year? Then that's fine!"

The sister-in-law happily repeated to the schoolteacher:

"Sir! Write it like this, from the fifteenth day of the first lunar month next year."

The great-grandfather also leaned over and said to the schoolteacher:

"Sir: write it clearly like this, take two sheng of rice today, and take the rest on the fifteenth day of the first lunar month next year."

"Oh! Like this. This... then what am I mortgaging to you for, great-grandfather! You really are..."

"I haven't done anything wrong. There's an old saying: 'One hand pays the money, the other hand delivers the goods.' And I'm not giving you two sheng of rice first. I'm not asking you for the one dou I lent you before."

The schoolteacher put down his glasses and wiped the snot on his mustache, looking a little embarrassed:

"How should I write it then?"

"Sir! Don't write it, I won't mortgage it to him like this." The sister-in-law turned pale, picked up Xiu Zhen who was comforting the crying child, put the nipple into the child's mouth, and squeezed the empty breast desperately with one hand.

The mother had already come out and heard the news, and she did not approve of mortgaging the only ancestral property to others.

"I'll go borrow fourteen copper coins from old lady Zhonggui, and she'll always ask me to chant Buddha's name later, which can be deducted from the chanting wages. If I can borrow it, I'll go weigh a jin of flour." The mother walked away, and the children watched her retreating figure and continued to cry. (To be continued)

Legal Advice 178

Question

After my husband passed away, the property was divided and a division agreement was established. I only have one adopted daughter under my care. If I remarry, to whom will the property of my late husband belong? Before the remarriage, can I freely sell it, or will it be exclusively enjoyed by my adopted daughter? If the property can be exclusively enjoyed by my adopted daughter, what procedures should I follow to determine her property rights? If the above two methods cannot be achieved, I am willing to donate all the property and deeds to a charity for good deeds. I wonder if anyone will object? Shou Yuan asks.

Answer

When you remarry, the property inherited from your late husband still belongs to you and you can dispose of it freely. You can either keep it for yourself, give it to your adopted daughter, or donate it to a charitable organization, all of which are permissible. Answered by Lawyer Pu Shunqing (This lawyer's correspondence address: No. 4 Yiyu Lane, Route Lafayette, Shanghai)

Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Talks

"Re-Discussion" of the Issue of Coeducation 179

— Zhe Yong

Mayor Yuan of Beiping, based on his personal views, stood out amidst the national craze for reading classics and honoring Confucius by banning middle schools in Beiping. It is truly astonishing that an administrative head of a city could change the educational system with his own determination. Subsequently, several reports in the newspapers indicated that the Ministry of Education had issued instructions regarding the separation of schools for boys and girls in Beiping, but we still do not know what these instructions are. Therefore, we dare not speculate on what attitude the highest educational administrative agency in the country takes on the issue of coeducation.

However, I feel that the issue of coeducation still has value that is worth re-discussing. We examine it from a historical perspective: In feudal society, women were only in a subordinate position to men. People generally believed that women's intelligence was lower than that of men, so they were judged to be men's playthings or should be men's slaves. The empresses and concubines of emperors and princes belonged to the former, while the wives and concubines of commoners belonged to the latter. After the era entered the capitalist system, women, awakened by the times, were no longer willing to be men's playthings or slaves. As a result, countless small birds of Holm flew out of the puppet family's prison, demanding the equality endowed by nature, demanding economic equality in occupations. This era was our May Fourth era, so schools opened their doors to women, and women participated in all sectors of industry and commerce, and female officials were also active in politics. When this era broke out of the feudal atmosphere, although it encountered great resistance, this resistance ultimately could not resist the great power of that era!

The struggle for coeducation seemed to have ended in the May Fourth era, and it did indeed make people generally understand that male and female education should be equal. But today, twenty years later, to have us drag that dead issue out of the grave for discussion again, I think it would not be a bad thing if it could re-evaluate its value.

Clearly, the reason why the gentlemen who advocate separate schools for boys and girls do not approve of coeducation is that they believe that coeducation is related to social morality, not to make further changes to the educational curriculum based on gender.

Men and women who had just shed the cloak of feudal thought, like girls who had just unbound their feet, often felt awkward and uneasy when walking. Similarly, because the initial concept of the opposite sex among coeducational students was nurtured from the mysterious phenomenon of gender separation in feudalism, there were inevitably more disputes among men and women after liberation. However, this was still because the feudal era made the knowledge of sexuality between men and women too mysterious. We dare to believe that if we give it time and break down all the mystery between men and women, wouldn't men and women still be the same and not that strange? There is evidence that Bebel, in his book "Woman and Socialism," mentioned that the men and women of Sparta had played together naked from childhood, and did not have any mysterious ideas about sexual physiology, but it was not seen that they often caused sexual impulses as a result. Therefore, Bebel also said in the chapter "Woman and Intelligence" that coeducation will never cause male students to abandon their studies due to the temptation of women. On the contrary, precisely because of mutual competition, they strive for honor in front of the opposite sex and work harder and more diligently. May I ask, what relationship does coeducation have with social morality? If it is said that studying in the same room will cause sexual impulses, is that not a joke? If it is said that more opportunities to contact the opposite sex will easily cause social morality problems, then students may have more opportunities to contact the opposite sex outside of school classrooms. In this way, the problem of social morality will be impossible to prevent. Therefore, instead of fundamentally guiding men and women to recognize

proper sexual knowledge, but mystifying it and sealing it off, this is a method of abandoning the fundamental and pursuing the superficial, and the result must be a return to the era of feudal thought!

The opportunity for male and female education should be equal, I think no one will object to this premise, but separate schools for boys and girls is tantamount to adding another chain of iron to prevent equality in the case where the opportunity for male and female education is not yet equal. Try to investigate the ratio of male to female students in any school, and it has never reached an equal ratio. Even female students are just a decoration in the school, and it is still far from matching the number of male students. It can be seen that the actual equality of opportunity for male and female education has still not been achieved. In this transitional era, the only right way is to advocate increasing the enrollment of female students. But before the equality in form has been achieved, the order for separate schools has been issued. Only a few girls' schools are set up in the city, and the number is very different compared to the number of boys' schools. This is actually no different from judging the reduction of women's educational opportunities.

I say that the issue of coeducation is worth re-discussing, but what is worth re-discussing is: Should male and female education be consistent? Should there be a part of the difference in the courses received by men and women? But it is not the issue of separate schools for boys and girls. It is a research problem for educators and psychologists, but not a social morality problem worried about by administrative officials.

Training and Cultivation

Body and Soul 180

— Yaqing

The question of the relationship between body and soul, spirit and matter, has been discussed since the dawn of human society. Primitive humans, lacking any scientific knowledge, not only did not understand general natural phenomena, but were also baffled by many phenomena of human physiology and life itself. First and foremost, death puzzled them. In their eyes, when a living person died, their body remained, and the position of their five senses and limbs did not change in the slightest, but their breathing ceased, which was fundamentally different from when they were alive: This was simply a strange thing! From this, they developed a hypothesis: when a person is alive, there must be something that governs their body, and when they die, that thing that governs their body leaves them and goes elsewhere; this thing they called the soul. They believed that the human body was merely a shell, controlled by the soul, and once the soul departed, the person immediately died, and therefore their body had no function; it was the soul that determined the existence of the body, not the body that determined the existence of the soul. Thus, primitive humans formed the belief in the immortality of the soul. This belief was not only supported by the fact that the body did not change when a person died, but also by the more ample evidence of their often seeing dead people in their dreams. They thought, a person has already died, their body has already decayed, why can living people still meet them in their dreams? Isn't this ironclad proof of the immortality of the soul?

Primitive humans also held the same unscientific understanding of sleep. Because people often replay their daytime life in dreams during sleep, such as primitive savages hunting during the day, chasing bison, or fighting with other groups, these things would inevitably be fragmentarily replayed in dreams. Primitive humans believed this to be the action of the soul leaving the body, so they were convinced that the soul could act independently of the body; if it were not so, then how could the body be sleeping here without any movement, while oneself was chasing bison or fighting with others in the wild?

The soul can exist independently of the body and is perpetually immortal: this is the understanding of primitive humans regarding the question of the relationship between body and soul. Due to this understanding, many superstitious beliefs and behaviors of mankind have been formed. According to Lafargue's research, many savages even believe that their body's shadow is their soul, and therefore attach great importance to their shadow. In his famous "The Evolution of the Idea of Justice," he said: "The savages of Epuateu, at noon, because their body has no shadow, do not leave their huts, fearing to lose their soul, even to the point of death. The Greeks also had a similar idea. They believed that those who passed through the temple of Lykaion would lose their shadow and return to death. The image of a person reflected in clear water or on a smooth plane is the image of his soul; if you hit it, you will hurt the soul. The ancient anecdote of Narcissus, and the wax figure curses of medieval magic, are probably linked to this belief. If you remove or move a person's portrait, it is like taking away their soul. For this reason, savages refuse to be portrayed." In fact, not only are there such phenomena among savages, but the development of this belief in "immortality of the soul" can also be seen everywhere in our society. Such as chanting scriptures for the dead, holding memorial services for departed souls, such as grand funerals, venerating ancestors, and superstitious phenomena such as believing in ghosts and gods, are they not all developed from the belief in "immortality of the soul"?

However, with the development of society and human knowledge, mankind has increasingly had a more scientific understanding of all natural and life phenomena. Such as the phenomena of the natural world, are merely the physical manifestations of chemical and physical laws, without any God ruling there.

Page 22

宰; All phenomena in the process of human life, such as diseases and death, such as dreams, etc., can only be found in sociology and physiology for correct explanation, and the "immortality of the soul" is useless here. --These have all been known to mankind since the flourishing of science in the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries. However, even in this era when science has been quite developed, in human society, regarding the understanding of the relationship between body and soul, in addition to some people still holding the primitive belief in "immortality of the soul", there are also some people who call themselves scientists and thinkers who hold mechanistic views; Although this view is more advanced than the "immortality of the soul", it is still wrong, so it must be criticized.

According to mechanists, a person is like a machine that can move; besides having a machine-like body, there is nothing else. Therefore, things like soul, energy, spirit, in their view, do not exist at all, and therefore have no effect in the process of human life. It is true that a soul that is independent of the body as understood by savages does not exist, but if we understand "soul" as "energy" or "spirit", then it does exist. It is just that such a soul does not exist in isolation, but is dependent on the body; it is the body that determines the existence of the soul, not the soul that determines the existence of the body.

With the development of society, human energy is also developing day by day. Now, human intelligence and creativity are several times higher than those of primitive people; people must admit that although people in the twentieth century and people in the primitive era are both human, their wisdom, energy, and soul are not the same: the former is much higher than the latter. From this, we cannot deny the existence and function of the "soul" or "spirit", but this existence is attached to the body. Furthermore, taking an individual as an example, a person not only has a body, but also has their spirit and soul; ultimately, this spirit, this soul, is naturally dependent on the body, but an upward or fallen soul also has a certain reaction on a person's life and even on the entire society. In fact, in our society, there are many people who, in order to live in Western-style houses, eat elaborate dishes, and play with women, indulge their bodies in the abyss of extravagance and debauchery, and do not hesitate to specialize in flattering, fabricating rumors and falsehoods, selling themselves and harming others. People like this, their souls are of course fallen, and can even be said to be walking corpses without souls, and their impact on human society will of course be harmful; conversely, there is another kind of people who are always responsible for the truth, "cannot be moved by wealth and status, cannot be subdued by force", never say things that they themselves consider wrong, and never do things that they themselves consider wrong: This kind of person can be called a person with a great soul, and their impact on human society is of course also promoting. I think that under the current circumstances of "the world is getting worse", "morality is declining", and "credit is bankrupt", everyone, especially young people, must pay attention to maintaining their own pure and great souls, and be ashamed to be associated with walking corpses!

However, I am not asking everyone to pay no attention to material life at all, and not to seek the material things necessary for their lives to maintain the existence of their bodies, and to talk emptily about "great souls"; no, that is a mysterious and abstract high-sounding tune, and can even be said to be the development of primitive superstitious ideas, and we do not make such a proposition. We believe that maintaining life and maintaining an individual's great soul do not conflict, as long as you do not have excessive material desires. Naturally, people always want their material life to get better day by day, but people who value their personality and have a clear understanding of objective truth do not only want their individual life to get better day by day, they mainly strive to make the material life of the general society get better day by day; therefore, in times of emergency, they would rather sacrifice their bodies than sell their souls to harm human society: This is the kind of person with a great soul that we praise, and this kind of person is what we should and can do.

Outlying Postal Agencies

Roar, Pengtian River! 181

— Kuoching

Kunming Correspondence

The Pengyin River is about seven miles from Tangluo in the undetermined area between Yunnan and Burma. The source of the river comes from the Kumen Ridge, and the western branch flows into the Mai Likai River. About a mile from the Pengyin River, you can already hear the sound of the surging river, which is truly thrilling, simply roaring like an army of thousands chasing the enemy. If one is a timid person, I believe one would definitely not want to get close to such a terrifying sound.

In winter, the river is completely dry, but after the spring rains, the streams from the four mountains converge into this river, and then the river is full. The river is more than a mile wide, and the banks are full of grotesque rocks. Some look like they are lying down or squatting, some are lined up on the shore like guards, some are pillars in the middle of the river like one man guarding the pass, and some lie across the heart of the river, where the rapid current rushes and makes the sound of the weak resisting. The turquoise river rolls eastward, set against the lush green high mountains and the towering peaks that stand alone and pierce the clouds. Such beautiful scenery can definitely not be appreciated by people elsewhere. We often wandered there, singing the song "Beautiful China" boldly, and would not want to leave until the sun urged us.

I once naively thought about building a thatched hut there, wandering by the river all day long, reading the books of the ancients as much as possible, sadly expressing the songs of the heart, quietly avoiding the troubles of the world, and living a leisurely life, free from strife with the world, working at sunrise and resting at sunset, living the life of primitive people, but this is a dream that can never be realized, this heavy burden will not allow me to be lazy or to shirk responsibility. But then I thought, if ordinary dignitaries were to see such good scenery, perhaps they would have the idea of "I will enter the mountains and travel with Chisongzi," and living beings could suffer less misery.

The Pengyin River has a large iron cable bridge built by the British, which is more than twenty feet long and eight feet wide. The iron cable is twisted together from many fine iron wires, forming an iron rope as thick as a head. There are a total of six iron ropes, two are erected on the top of the bridge, and four are placed at the bottom of the bridge. The two ends of the iron rope are deeply buried in the soil and stone on both banks, and then wooden boards are laid flat on the four iron ropes on the bottom surface one by one, and the upper and lower sides are connected with iron bars as thick as fingers, and the iron bars are nailed to the wooden boards with nails, thus a top iron cable bridge is successfully built. This iron cable bridge is much stronger than a rope bridge and more convenient than a zipline bridge, so many bridges there are built with iron cables.

Not far from crossing the Pengyin River, about five miles away, is a village. All of them are wild people, and they mostly carry weapons such as knives and spears on their shoulders, and carry bamboo baskets on their backs to transport things, wearing short clothes made of printed cloth, with some wearing pants and some wearing a skirt on their lower body. The women also carry bamboo baskets on their backs, wear short clothes and long skirts, and wear amber ear studs or two pairs of shackles on their ears. Men, women, old and young all like to chew raw gambier, and they use lipstick as beauty, so everyone has a blood basin-like mouth. Once, when we approached them, they and they all looked at us with surprised eyes.

"Ah! Where did these people come from?" they mumbled in their local language. I just stared at them blankly. One of our companions who understood their language replied to them: "We are here to play, and we also plan to give you some things as a greeting gift." As he spoke, he took out the needles, brocade, local cloth, old cloth, tobacco, etc. that we had specially prepared, and gave each of them a copy.

As they were talking, the sun was only a glimmer of light, so I opened the mirror and wanted to take advantage of the opportunity to take a photo, but they suddenly ran away, and the panicked state was really like they had discovered the enemy or encountered a man-eating tiger or leopard.

"This is something that captures people's souls, you are all high officials of the Celestial Dynasty, how can you do such illegal things?" They negotiated with one of our companions in their local language.

"No, we are not high officials, this is taking a photo. If you take a photo, there will be a piece of paper inside that will show your shape on that paper." My companion said.

No matter how you explained it, they would never allow us to photograph them. Before long, the sun had already hidden in the clouds, and this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity was finally lost in this way.

In this village, there is only one Han Chinese family, and they run a small shop specializing in selling groceries. In such a remote place, among thousands of wild people, to find a few Han Chinese is such a happy thing! They, almost assimilated with the wild people, only because their ancestors passed down the story that they were Han Chinese, so they never admitted that they were natives, but said that they were Han Chinese. They only knew that they moved there during the Ming Dynasty, when there was an emperor, so they also asked us: "What dynasty is it now? Who is sitting on the throne?" We told them in detail, but they just listened like they were listening to a story, and they didn't believe that China had no emperor. Finally, he cried bitterly, saying that they were being invaded because they had lost the protection of their motherland. When they cried bitterly, we were also sighing, grieving for the fate of the motherland.

They don't know spring, summer, autumn, and winter, they only know that when the wild flowers bloom, it is spring, when the sun is like a fiery umbrella, it is summer, when the grain and rice are harvested, it is autumn, and when the white snow is flying in the sky, it is winter, and the first day of the new rice being harvested is considered New Year's Day.

Another time, we went to play at a native's house, and they were brightly lit and celebrating the New Year, with many dishes arranged on the table, including fish, beast meat, etc. When we walked into their house, they welcomed us very much, and they thought it was a very exciting thing to meet a Han Chinese on New Year's Day. After we sat down, we drank their homemade white wine, the taste of which could definitely not be bought anywhere else.

Halfway through the drinking, the host stood up and gave a speech, looking very serious. His sons, daughters, grandsons, and granddaughters all listened quietly. I just stared blankly, not knowing what kind of story he was telling. Later, our companion translated it for us, and we learned that he said this:

"Listen to me! We were all descendants of Meng Huo. That year, Zhuge Wuhou conquered the south, and Meng Huo was defeated and captured. Thanks to Wuhou not killing him, we have today. So we thank Wuhou, and we should thank the Han Chinese even more, because Wuhou is a Han Chinese. We have been receiving Han favors for generations, so from now on we should remember that the Han Dynasty is our benefactor."

They have been passing this down from generation to generation, and every New Year's Day, the head of the family announces it to his children and grandchildren. Therefore, they still remember China firmly, even under the rule of imperialists, they still do not forget China.

According to our companion: "There are all high mountains and steep ridges, so the natives make a living by planting rice fields. Their cultivation method is to let it grow and bear fruit on its own. If they can be taught planting methods, then the harvest will definitely not be just this little bit. Because life can still be lived, this has developed the habit of being lazy. Other products there include animal skins, musk, deer antler, lacquer, medicinal materials, sesame, etc.; tea is also produced there, with a strong flavor, but unfortunately no one cares about it now. What is produced on the ground is so abundant, as for what is underground, it is even more spectacular, and if it is developed, there will definitely be very surprising developments. As for all the customs of the natives, they are almost the same as those of the Han Chinese."

Amateur Study

A Humble Opinion on the Problem of Amateur Further Study 182

— Huang Chen

I think that if one is a progressive professional, no matter what kind of person in the business world, from the factory director and manager to the worker and apprentice, they will all feel the pain of not having enough knowledge. The main reasons are no more than five: 1. In the period of schooling, due to poor family circumstances or sudden changes in economic conditions, they dropped out of school midway and had to embark on a professional path; 2. Because of insufficient effort during the period of schooling, their acquisition of knowledge was not substantial; 3. Because they did not affirm their future path during the period of schooling, they did not use what they learned; 4. Because of the relationship between professional interests and other unavoidable reasons, they changed careers midway, resulting in a very lack of knowledge of the new profession; 5. Because they have been in the industry for a long time, they lack opportunities for further study, or they study further without good guidance, resulting in panic about knowledge.

Professionals are urgently in need of opportunities for further study, the reason being: on the one hand, they can relieve the hunger for the above-mentioned intellectual desire, and on the other hand, they can remedy the defects in their business with the results of the knowledge they have acquired, and further seek to improve their business. However, in fact, can the wishes of these professionals be truly satisfied? Needless to say, this is very pitiful. Of course, the government is worried that it will not be able to sustain the surface relief of the recent decline of industry and commerce, and will definitely not think of the smaller problems considered by politicians, such as the amateur further study of industrialists and businessmen. Educators, for these professionals, that is, the students of previous educators, are like daughters who have been married off and water that has been poured out, and no longer pay attention to or care about them. Thus, after a few years, the common people will often fall behind the later competitors. This is not only a luxury and waste of talent cultivation in a country, but also the biggest obstacle to not being able to compete successfully with other countries.

Some people say that starting a business is difficult, but maintaining it is even more difficult. I also say that it is not easy to cultivate talent, and it is even more difficult to prevent the already cultivated talent from becoming corrupt. Therefore, I dare to loudly call for the opinions and specific measures of "promoting amateur further study" and "broadly seeking opportunities for further study for professionals" before people in society:

1. Build Large-Scale Amateur Libraries

Although further study is not limited to books, we can affirm that books are indeed the results of research or experience accumulated by predecessors. Although learning can be known after practice, knowing before practice, or knowing and practicing at the same time, is not necessarily a more convenient method for our time-saving professionals. However, the economic ability of most professionals themselves is very weak. Not to mention the limited ability to support a family, even the ability to support themselves is unreliable. How can they bear the debt of buying books again? Therefore, we cannot but hand over this responsibility to the public libraries of society. However, the current state of public libraries, except for a few facilities in remote rural areas, even in cities, most of them are abnormally simple, or too specialized (such as focusing on social sciences or literature departments), or too focused on low-level interests (such as displaying picture magazines with various women's photos), and most of them are not suitable for the reading of the vast number of professionals.

I believe that in addition to basic items, a more standard amateur library should list various professional departments, from shallow to deep, in a progressive style, to accommodate different levels of intellectual ability and various aspects of theory or skills.

Page 23

This is naturally a more troublesome task, but I dare say that if these points cannot be achieved, this library will still not be able to universally meet the different needs of general professionals.

2. Open University Lectures

Now, whether in China or abroad, university lectures seem to be mostly the monopoly of special classes. In form, it seems like a proud noblewoman, and ordinary people cannot obtain even the desire to have a close look at her beauty. Is there a need to revise this system? I think it is worth discussing. The academic itself is indeed noble, but the application of the academic should be as popular as possible. The academic cannot only be used by a few capitalists, but should tend to the souls of the masses. I heard that Cambridge, England already has this atmosphere, and there are several courses that can be specially selected for amateur listeners. This is a good method that can be imitated. I advocate opening all lectures in various universities to allow professionals who are determined to conduct in-depth research to study freely. I think these free researchers, they do not come for diplomas, they may be more effective than college students who go to university to spend their years as dormitories.

3. Establish Amateur Further Study Guidance Centers

The existing "mailboxes", "consultants", etc., which are similar in nature to guidance, are mostly narrow in scope and confined to the circle of common sense, and are really not enough to meet the desires of professionals who have various different needs. Therefore, I advocate establishing a complete amateur further study guidance center, which not only guides how to study further, but also has the responsibility of explaining difficulties. The guidance personnel should be broadly recruited from domestic academics and entrepreneurs to be responsible for the duties. For the sake of convenience, they can be attached to famous universities or famous amateur libraries.

The above three points are essential plans for the purpose of promoting the further study of general professionals, enriching the knowledge and skills of industrialists and businessmen, and developing their business. However, this matter is of great importance. If it can attract jade by throwing bricks and make society and the government pay attention to this, then the writing of this article may not be in vain!

Amateur Coffee Shop

On Humor 183

— Ze

The two characters for "humor" (滑稽) are not a recent invention; they have existed since ancient times. Figures like Dongfang Shuo and Chunyu Kun were known in ancient texts as "humorous individuals." However, the so-called humor of the past seems to differ from that of the present. Humorous predecessors like Dongfang Shuo and Chunyu Kun primarily used indirect arguments, sophistry, or metaphorical language to remonstrate with rulers and challenge scholars. The modern understanding of humor, however, has a sense of making people feel lighthearted and laugh. According to the current common interpretation of humor, it is the opposite of solemnity and seriousness and does not evoke feelings of tragedy or indignation; the feeling it gives people is relaxed and pleasant. Aristotle, in his "Poetics," said, "Humor is a defect or ugliness that does not involve pain or disaster." Although this is the saying of an ancient Greek philosopher, it also contains the meaning that we recognize today: humor is the opposite of solemnity and seriousness and can make people laugh.

What constitutes various forms of humor is mostly trivial matters of human life. According to general observation, humor can be roughly divided into the following categories: First, humor inherent in excessively abnormal and grotesque figures, such as the small-headed man at the Shanghai City God Temple, the world's largest fat man weighing over seven hundred pounds, and dwarfs less than two feet tall, are humorous things that make people burst into laughter at first sight. Second, humor composed of extremely disharmonious and disproportionate things, such as the disharmonious expression of Granny Liu visiting the Grand View Garden as depicted in "Dream of the Red Chamber," and the exaggeratedly made-up male actors playing female roles in traditional Chinese operas, are examples of this category of humor. Third, the unexpected and unusual things that possess humor: For example, if there were a modern young man walking hand in hand with a completely traditionally dressed, bound-footed woman on Nanjing Road, the scene would probably make even the most composed person laugh until their stomach ached. Also, as everyone knows, Laurel and Hardy, known as "a pair of living treasures," often do all kinds of unexpected and clumsy things on the screen to make the general audience laugh, which is why they have become comedic stars. These two are concrete illustrations of this category of humor.

As for the humor we express in our conversations and writings, it generally contains one of these two meanings: First, it can stimulate people's sexual feelings; second, it has a satirical meaning. Because everyone has a sexual instinct and a desire to satisfy sexual desires, it is easiest to create humorous and funny words and stories in the relationship between men and women. In rural areas and among ordinary laborers, this kind of humorous and interesting story is the most popular. As for humor with a satirical meaning, good examples can be found in the words of general orators and eloquent speakers, and in the works of some literary writers. For example, Gogol's "The Quarrel of the Two Ivans" and "The Government Inspector," Wu Jingzi's "The Scholars," and Li Boyuan's "A Record of Officialdom Exposed," all have a spicy satirical meaning and a humorous and funny tone. Now, let us randomly quote a passage from "The Scholars" for reference!

"...The two (Zhang Jingzhai and Fan Jin) came in. First, Jingzhai paid his respects, and Fan Jin came forward to perform the ritual between teacher and student. Magistrate Tang repeatedly declined and offered them tea. He chatted with Jingzhai about their long separation and praised Fan Jin's articles, asking, "Why didn't you go to the metropolitan examination?" Fan Jin then said, "My late mother passed away, and I am observing mourning according to the regulations." Magistrate Tang was shocked and hurriedly ordered to change into auspicious clothing. He escorted them to the back hall and set out wine... The magistrate sat down, and the tableware used were all inlaid with silver. Fan Jin hesitated to pick up the cup and chopsticks. The magistrate did not understand why. Jingzhai smiled and said, "Mr. Shi is observing mourning according to the regulations and probably won't use these cups and chopsticks." The magistrate hurriedly ordered them to be replaced. He replaced them with a porcelain cup and a pair of ivory chopsticks, but Fan Jin still refused to use them. Jingzhai said, "These chopsticks are also not to be used." He then replaced them with a pair of white bamboo chopsticks, and only then was it over. The magistrate wondered, "He is so respectful in his mourning that perhaps he doesn't use meat or wine, but I didn't prepare any." Later, he saw him pick a large shrimp meatball from the bird's nest bowl and put it in his mouth, and then he felt relieved..."

What is expressed here is not only humorous and funny but also contains a spicy satirical meaning.

Because humor can make people laugh easily, and what is contained in general words often contains a satirical meaning, in our conversations and in our writings, if we are good at using humorous satirical words, and good at expressing humorous things with a satirical flavor, it can have unexpected effects. However, this is a very difficult thing to do well. First of all, we must know the objective meaning of humor. That is to say, whether a sentence or a thing is humorous depends mainly on your audience and readers, and cannot be based entirely on your subjective arbitrariness; it is necessary for what you subjectively consider humorous to coincide with what is objectively considered humorous. More specifically, it is necessary that what you find funny, your audience or readers also find funny, in order to have an effect, otherwise it will cause people to dislike it. In general chatting and bragging, we often see some people who are not lively and do not understand humor, pretending to be lively and humorous, giving long humorous jokes, but as a result, in addition to laughing alone, other people not only do not laugh, but also feel bored and feel that it is a bit of a killjoy. Such inconsistent expressions of subjective humor and objective humor not only fail to produce the effect of humor but also reveal the "humorist's" ineptitude. Furthermore, the expression of humor should also avoid vulgarity and frivolousness, that is to say, humor should have profound social significance and should not be composed of trivial and low-level things. Only such humor can produce a meaningful satirical effect and be beneficial to oneself and human society; otherwise, it will not only make oneself a clown, despised and played with, but also trivialize many serious issues, preventing the truth from being revealed.

At the same time, the expression of humor should also be limited and not humorous at any time and in any place. Because no matter what, even if it is humor with great satire, it is not very serious, and therefore it hinders the formal resolution of the problem. Imagine, if you only satirize and express humor no matter what happens, such as when someone in another family dies, or when the country is in danger, wouldn't that be too unreasonable! I think only those noble ladies who are tired of material life specialize in pursuing humorous interests to kill the long years; only those clowns who specialize in relying on women for food and clothing specialize in talking about humor and studying humor; ordinary people who live seriously, even if they want to say a little humorous word and say a little humorous thing, are limited and have a meaningful meaning.

Miscellaneous Writings

Tolstoy's Humanitarianism 184

— Shao Wen

Tolstoy is not only a world-renowned writer but also the most famous humanitarian. Because his humanitarian teachings contain many truths, and because he has great artistic talent, the influence of his humanitarianism and the value of his works are very great.

First of all, what is worth our attention is his famous "On Art." I think the value of this work is above many other books on "Introduction to Art." In this, Tolstoy has put forward many propositions that our "new" literary researchers have not thought of, and has said many things that many "new people" dare not say now. He has opposed various idealistic views of art in strong language, he has boldly pointed out the hypocrisy of the lives and art of the upper classes, and he has striven to praise the lives and art of the general working masses, showing his just and zealous attitude of loving truth. But we should understand that Tolstoy expresses all his opinions from the standpoint of Christianity and from the standpoint of humanitarianism. After refuting idealistic theories and vehemently criticizing the lives and art of the upper classes, he clearly put forward the proposition that religious thought determines the value of art. He said:

"The evaluation of the characteristics of art (that is, the emotion it conveys) is closely related to man's understanding of the meaning of life and the happiness or unhappiness of life as he sees it. The happiness or unhappiness of life is entirely determined by religion."

Under such a religious view of art, he also combined his doctrine of "non-resistance to evil" with art. According to him, only those works that can make the persecuted love their persecutors can be considered the greatest. He said:

"A noble work of art is not a temple of victory, with statues of victors, but a description of the human soul created in love, capable of making the robbed and killed pity and love his oppressor."

In this way, Tolstoy, while expressing great sympathy for the persecuted and being very "humane," ultimately wanted to make "the robbed and killed pity and love their oppressor" in order to preserve the position of the "oppressors."

The second half of the nineteenth century in Russia was precisely the time when the declining landed gentry used various cruel methods to deal with the general Russian people in order to maintain their rule. At this time, Tolstoy put forward the proposition of "non-resistance to evil," his reason being: "Because fire cannot extinguish fire, water cannot dry water, and evil cannot be eradicated by evil." But if this were really the case, then all the evil deeds of the Russian landed gentry at that time would not be resisted, and their position would not be questioned. From this, we can say that Tolstoy's teachings, his view of art, and his humanitarianism are all reflections of the consciousness of a certain section of the landed gentry of Russia at that time.

Needless to say, Tolstoy's many literary works were also written under his view of art and his humanitarianism. Therefore, the central consciousness expressed in his literary works is fundamentally the consciousness of a section of the landed gentry. It is true that Tolstoy, the religious figure and humanitarian, was a great realist writer who, in his many literary creations, used the realist method of depiction to ruthlessly expose the decadent lives and evil deeds of the landlords and aristocrats. For example, in "The Kingdom of God Is Within You," he ruthlessly exposed the cruel oppression of peasants by officials, in "What Then Must We Do?" he truthfully showed the close relationship between the entertainment of the upper classes and the suffering of the people, and in "I Cannot Be Silent" he described the cruelty of those who dealt with peasants with the death penalty... However, he was talking about these things from the moral sins of the landlords and aristocrats

Continued on page 5

Page 24

Page 25

to explain these things, and did not actually describe them; he did not advocate that "the robbed and killed" resist their "oppressors," but instead asked them to "pity and love" their "oppressors," hoping that those "oppressors" - the landlords and aristocrats - would reform and do good. His such efforts "are nothing more than the most cunning, and therefore the most detestable, cultivation of clericalism."

Due to the development of capitalism, the Russian countryside at the end of the nineteenth century suffered irreparable destruction. In this destruction, not only the landlords and aristocrats felt uneasy, but also the suffering in the lives of the general peasants was increasingly deepened. Thus, imperceptibly, peasants and a section of landlords stood on the same front in opposing urban capitalism. Thus, the humanitarian Tolstoy also reflected in his works the consciousness of the landlords and peasants, hating the city, opposing capitalism, and praising the simple countryside. - From this point of view, it can also be seen that Tolstoy's worldview and his humanitarianism are aristocratic.

Announcement: Wu Shide, Yi Ren, Yu Min, You Quan, Yang Hua, Ke Cong, Xin Zi, Zhong Minyi, Bo, gentlemen, your works kindly submitted in July are greatly appreciated! Manuscript fees have been settled clearly. Please bring your receipt with your seal to the accounting department of this publication between the 6th and 10th, and 16th and 20th of each month (excluding Sundays) from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM to collect the fees. (Sincerely, the Editorial Department of Shen Bao Amateur Weekly)

Special Report

Overseas Chinese Around the World (5) 185

— Zhong Minyi

Burma

Burma borders Thailand to the east and is located south of the Yunnan-Sichuan border region of our country. There are approximately 300,000 overseas Chinese here, most of whom are skilled workers, merchants, and coolies. Since Britain annexed Burma in 1895, the influence of overseas Chinese in Burma has been greatly hit, but until the outbreak of the European War, the influence of overseas Chinese in Burma was developing day by day. They did business and worked in places like Yangon and could earn some money every year, and many of them had become wealthy. At the same time, in addition to running their own businesses, overseas Chinese in Burma also strived to establish schools and newspapers to develop overseas Chinese education and culture. But since the outbreak of the European War, the situation has become increasingly different from before. First, because Britain incited the Burmese to exclude overseas Chinese, our compatriots in Burma were greatly hit; second, because the power of Indian Chettiars (Indian moneylenders) was increasingly developing in Burma, the lower-level merchants among the overseas Chinese had to rely on them to maintain their livelihoods, and in fact, the inherent position of overseas Chinese in Burma had been replaced by the Chettiars; at the same time, the financial power of European and American countries was also increasingly penetrating Burma. There are now more than a dozen banks from seven countries in Yangon, all with strong capital and well-organized. However, there is only one bank in Yangon that belongs to Chinese nationality, and its capital is not very strong, so it is naturally unable to compete with others in business. In this way, since Burma's finances are in the hands of foreigners, its industry and commerce cannot compete with others, and it is also openly excluded by the Burmese, how can the influence of overseas Chinese in Burma not decline day by day?

Vietnam

Vietnam is located in the south of China and is connected to provinces such as Guangdong, Guangxi, and Yunnan. We usually call it Annam, and foreigners call it French Indochina. As early as the Qin and Han dynasties, Vietnam was once an internal territory of China; the Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties also regarded China as the suzerain. It was not until the Sino-French Treaty of 1885 was signed that Vietnam changed from a territory of China to a French colony. There are no exact statistics on how many overseas Chinese there are here: some say 400,000, some say 600,000, and some say more than one million; but no matter what, the number of overseas Chinese in Vietnam is at least 700,000 or 800,000. Most of them are from Guangdong and Fujian. On October 16, 1906, in order to facilitate its rule, the French government divided the overseas Chinese in Cochinchina into five groups based on their differences in origin and language and had them live in five districts. The so-called five groups are Guangzhou, Fujian, Hainan, Chaozhou, and Hakka.

Most of the people from Guangzhou in Vietnam are engaged in industry and commerce. In Saigon and other places, rice shops, timber shops, cloth shops, brick and tile manufacturing, lime manufacturing, fur, animal bones, and other industries are all operated by Cantonese people. In addition, carpenters, stonemasons, tailors, bootmakers, and butchers are also mostly Cantonese. Although the number of people from Fujian in this area is relatively small, their influence in industry and commerce is very great. Factories and rice shops in places like Cholon are mostly opened by them. According to surveys, there are more than 30 rice milling factories in Saigon, of which those operated by overseas Chinese account for as many as 28 or 29, and Fujianese account for the largest number in these 28 or 29. Hakka overseas Chinese are also mostly in Saigon and Cholon, and what they operate is mainly the tea industry; the Vietnamese tea industry is almost exclusively occupied by them. As for the Chaozhou people, most of them work as boatmen and coolies here, and those in the western provinces of Norodom also engage in agriculture.

Before France annexed Vietnam, overseas Chinese in Vietnam were treated quite favorably, and it was extremely convenient for Chinese people to go to Vietnam. Recently, the French have imposed various exorbitant taxes and levies on overseas Chinese in Vietnam, and even coolies and peddlers cannot avoid them. As for Chinese people going to Vietnam, they are made difficult in many ways: when entering the country, not only must they have their bodies checked and fingerprints taken, but they must also pay a certain amount of entry tax and body tax; if they are deemed to be slightly unsuitable, they will not be allowed to land, and even after landing, they are always in danger of being deported. Therefore, the fate of overseas Chinese in Vietnam is the same as that of overseas Chinese in other places: it is declining day by day.

The Philippines

The Philippines is a large island facing the Min and Yue provinces of our country across the sea, with an area of 120,000 square miles and a population of 11 million. As early as the Zhou and Qin dynasties, the Philippines and China already had exchanges. Many Filipinos are of mixed Chinese descent, and their agricultural tools, customs, and even the pronunciation of their names are very similar to those in China: these facts can fully prove the close relationship between China and the Philippines. (To be continued)

The Ice-Selling Child

They are both children, one runs around in the scorching sun all day because he is poor and his mother is sick. One is able to live a fairy-like life under the electric fan because he is rich and his parents love him. But the one who lives a fairy-like life often shouts that he is hot, while the one who runs around in the scorching sun does not complain or lament. What is the reason for this? Once the two meet, in the interaction, there is a different emotion that stirs everyone's heart.

A new work by children's literature writer Mr. Du Yemu, told by Mr. Du himself, is even more delicate and moving. (This broadcast will be in Shanghai dialect)

Movie News

Publishing World 189

The first issue of "The Singer Pictorial," which will shake the singing world, was published on August 1st as scheduled. The content is unusually rich, and each copy sells for only 20 cents. Major bookstores and newspaper vendors are selling it on commission. It is recently learned that in order to give preferential treatment to readers, the company is offering a subscription for all twelve issues of the year for only $1.80 during the period of soliciting basic subscribers. The subscription address is Singer Pictorial Society, Houde Lane Entrance, Tangjiawan, outside the Old West Gate. For a sample copy, please attach a 20-cent postage stamp and send it to the distribution department of the company, and it will be sent to the address provided.

The Ye Ye Society Will Perform "The Merry Widow" 190

The drama movement in this city can now be said to be very intense. In the past half year, it has almost become a world of drama. One step further, it can be said to be the year of drama. During this period, the Ye Ye Society, which dominated the north, has also announced its establishment on Father Labour Road in this city and has been registered with the Education Bureau. According to the society, it has a history of two years and has performed about twenty times without failure. It was first established in Beiping and then in Jinan. This organization was organized by Tu Qufei, the leader of the society's traveling troupe, together with Li Ruoshui, the director of the Ye Ye Drama Society's Shanghai office. The cast consists of sixteen or seventeen men and women, all of whom are from Beiping. The society is currently preparing very intensively. The first performance is said to be "The Merry Widow." The plot is extremely romantic and luxurious, and the costumes and sets are extremely magnificent, costing a great deal. It is currently in rehearsal and will soon be performed at the Jincheng Grand Theater. It is still a pioneering effort for a northern troupe to perform in Shanghai. At the time of the performance, there will be a different kind of spectacle. Ladies in Shanghai who love drama can enjoy a feast for the eyes.

Zhang Zhiyun Replays "The Peach Blossom Fan" 191

Former movie queen Zhang Zhiyun has recently changed her lifestyle, and her beautiful figure is rarely seen in social circles. However, those who visit her private residence see Zhang lightly powdered and dressed in plain clothes, with a naturally pure and elegant demeanor, and her charm is no less than in the past. Xinhua Film Company is producing "The Peach Blossom Fan" as a surprising move. In addition to recruiting dozens of major stars such as Jin Yan, Hu Ping, Tong Yuejuan, Wang Cilong, Gu Menghu, Dai Yanwan, and Zhang Zhizhi, the company is still lacking a suitable talent to play a certain important female role in the play. They discussed it with Zhang Zhiyun, who has agreed to appear on the screen in "The Peach Blossom Fan" as a guest performer.
